Their pervasion is only through knowledge but not through their essential nature (svarūpa).139 VV also quotes from the Lakṣmī Tantra and the Viṣṇupurāṇa of Parāśara in support of his view that Lakṣmī in all pervasive like the Lord.140

[[P89]] 77

Another characteristic of Lakṣmī which VV states in his work is her status as Puruṣakāra. This is possible on two grounds: Her vāllabhya (being the beloved of the Lord and Vātsalya (motherly action towards the living beings). When she acts as the Mediator and when the Lord becomes the upāya, she increases His qualities like Omniscience (jñāna) and Omnipotence (Śakti); and when the souls thus saved and liberated enjoy the Lord, Lakṣmī enhances the qualities such as saundarya and mādhurya of Her Lord.141

Vedānta Deśika (VD) in his commentary on the Catuśślokī and the Gadyatraya, in independent stotras and works like the Nyāyasiddhāñjana (NS) and Rahasyatrayasāra discusses the nature of Lakṣmī in a very elaborate manner. Of all these, His Catuḥślokī bhāṣya (CŚB) may said to be the most important because here he has summed up the entire range of thought on Lakṣmī depicted in a variety of texts. It is also worth noting in this context that being the advocate of the Vaḍagalai school, he has declared the following points regarding the nature and status of Lakṣmī.

  1. Śrī or Lakṣmī is coeval with Lord Viṣṇu at all aspects – svarūpa, rūpa, guṇa aiśvarya etc.

[[P90]] 78

  1. She is all-pervasive (vibhu) like the Lord himself and is therefore not aṇu like the rest of the creatures. She is, by the same token, not a jīva, not even a nityamukta.

  2. She is the most beloved of the Lord among His three consorts, the other two being Bhūmi and Nīḷā.

  3. She is the mother of all the living beings and is incapable of even a trace of nigraha (anger), being full of overwhelming love and compassion for them.

  4. It is for these reasons that she becomes the most effective Puruṣakāra between the Lord and the erring beings.

  5. Lakṣmī and Nārāyaṇa are associated eternally as an attribute and its substantive (Viśeṣaṇa and Viśeṣya).

  6. That is the reason why Lakṣmī can also be construed as the upāya, the means of liberation.

  7. Although she is not mentioned expressly in the first of the three major Mantras (called the Rahasyas) namely the Aṣṭākṣarī (OM Namo Nārāyaṇāya), her presence is implied in the personality of the Lord Himself referred

[[P91]] 79

to by the words ‘a’ (अ) and ’nāra’ forming part of this Tirumantra. In the second Rahasya, namely the Dvayamantra, Her presence is explicitly mentioned, suggesting that śaraṇāgati done to the Lord must be preceded by śaraṇāgati to Lakṣmī.

  1. By virtue of Her inseparable association with the Lord with whom she forms the Godhead, she becomes the śeṣiṇī along with Him who is the śeṣin, and as a couple they both constitute the upāya (means) and upeya (ultimate goal) of all the living beings.

  2. The spiritual quest of man comes to an end when he finds in this two-in-one ‘śeṣi’ couple, the recipient of all loving service (kaiṅkarya) which is divested of all feelings of ego. In other words, śeṣidaṁpatī alone is the summum bonum of all human life. Lakṣmī and Nārāyaṇa are conceived as two different beings functionally, but essentially and notionally ’they’ are but one single indivisible principle. The usage of the word ‘They’ here is only for the sake of referential convenience and is not a pointer to any dichotomy or duality in the ultimate Reality. The analogy given in the Pāñcarātrāgamas and in the Rāmāyaṇa for the relation between Lakṣmī and the Lord

[[P92]] 80

such as ‘rays and the Sun’, ’the beams and the Moon’, ’effulgence and the gem’ and ‘fragrance and the flower’ are all in support of this concept of the ultimate principle of ‘Lakṣmī-Nārāyaṇa-Dvandva’.

Broadly speaking, these are the ideas which we come across in the works of VD, sometimes briefly and sometimes elaborately. But as pointed out earlier, his commentary on Yāmuna’s Catuśślokī is of great value in arriving at his consummate view on the status of Lakṣmī.142

In the course of his commentary on the Catuśślokī, Deśika enumerates as many as eleven views regarding the nature, qualities, position and relation of Lakṣmī with the Brahman. Refuting these views, he comes out with five succinct statements on the status and nature of Lakṣmī which may be noted as follows:

The first view may be traced to the Teṅgalai school which accepts Lakṣmī as aṇu and as being dependent on the Lord, but enjoying special powers as distinguished from them.

The second concept is that she is different from all the three known well categories namely, Cit, Acit and Īśvara.

[[P93]] 81

The third view is that she belongs to the category of Īśvara, but the Lord alone can be the jagatkāraṇa and in this aspect she is only inferior to Him.

The fourth view could be the view entertained by Raṅganātha the commentator on the Śrīsūkta to which reference has already been made. According to him, both Lord and Lakṣmī equally enjoy the attributes such as Lordship. There is no contradiction here, because, their mutual consent opens up such as possibility.143

The fifth view which he expresses towards the end on the authority of Nārāyaṇa Muni, our author of the PM, is what Deśika himself actually subscribes to. According to this, Śrī is as pervasive as the Lord. She had become subordinate to Him. This subordination is voluntary but not obligatory because it takes place either by the free will of Lakṣmī or of her consort, or of both.

As the author of the Puruṣakāra Mīmāṁsā refers very often to VD and his works, and as Śrīśaileśa the commentator on the PM quotes profusely from a variety of texts of Deśika bearing upon this subject which will be analysed and studied

[[P94]] 82

in the course of this Thesis, Deśika’s views presented in those texts are not separately taken up for discussion in this chapter. The point that is worth taking up now is the Puruṣakāratva of Lakṣmī which is incidentally common to both the Vaḍagalai and Teṅgalai schools.

The term ‘Puruṣakāra’ is found employed in the Pāñcarātrāgamas such as the Viṣvaksena Saṁhitā. One unidentified Pāñcarātra text says:

अहंमत्प्राप्त्युपायो वै साक्षाल्लक्ष्मीपतिस्त्वयम्। लक्ष्मीः पुरुषकारेण वक्ष्मा प्राश्योजिनी।। एतस्याश्च विशेषोऽयं निगमान्तेषु शब्द्यते।।

The following passage is ascribed to the Viṣvaksena Saṁhitā where the term Puruṣakāra is employed.

आखिरग्रन्थैकधारणाः केचिद् भाग्याचिकाः पुनः। मत्पदाम्भोरुहद्वन्द्वं प्रपद्य प्रीतमानसाः।। लक्ष्मीं पुरुषकारेण वृतवन्तो वशनम्। मत्क्षणं प्राप्य सेनेत्रा प्राप्यं प्रापकमेव माम्। लब्ध्वा कृतार्थाः प्राप्स्यन्ते मामेवानन्द्यमानसाः।।

[[P95]] 83

Śrī Tirumaḻiśai Appāppaṅgār Svāmī, in his commentary Arumpadavilakkam on the Śrīvacanabhūṣaṇa of Piḷḷai Lokācārya explains the term ‘Puruṣakāra’ in four different ways in the “Prakaraṇavibhāga’. The word ‘Puruṣa’ refers to the Supreme Being Nārāyaṇa, and also to the jīva (individual soul). The etymology of the term is: ‘puruṣaṁ karoti iti puruṣakāraḥ’. With reference to the Supreme Being, the following three interpretations are possible:

  1. Puruṣaḥ pūrgatvāt puruṣaḥ (from the root ‘pṛ’ - pālanapūraṇayoḥ). Then the explanation would be: “bhagavantaṁ kṣamādipūrṇaṁ, ujjvalakāruṇyaviśiṣṭaṁ karoti iti puruṣakāraḥ”. To explain, Lakṣmī, by her intercession, brings out the latent virtues such as mercy and parental love belonging to the Lord, to a fuller display.

  2. Puruṣaḥ - ‘pālanāt puruṣaḥ’ (from the root ‘pṛ’ itself, in the sense of ‘pālana’ or protection). The explanation would then be: “bhagavantaṁ pālakaṁ, arthāt rakṣakaṁ karoti iti puruṣakāraḥ”. Lakṣmī makes the Lord ’the protector of the jīvas’.

[[P96]] 93

Śrī Tirumaḻiśai Appāppaṅgār Svāmī, in his commentary Arumpadavilakkam on the Śrīvacanabhūṣaṇa of Piḷḷai Lokācārya explains the term ‘Puruṣakāra’ in four different ways in the ‘Prakaraṇavibhāga’. The word ‘Puruṣa’ refers to the Supreme Being Nārāyaṇa, and also to the jīva (individual soul). The etymology of the term is: ‘puruṣaṁ karoti iti puruṣakāraḥ’. With reference to the Supreme Being, the following three interpretations are possible:

  1. Puruṣaḥ pūrgatvāt puruṣaḥ (from the root ‘pṛ’ - pālanapūraṇayoḥ). Then the explanation would be: “bhagavantaṁ kṣamādipūrṇaṁ, ujjvalakāruṇyaviśiṣṭaṁ karoti iti puruṣakāraḥ”. To explain, Lakṣmī, by her intercession, brings out the latent virtues such as mercy and parental love belonging to the Lord, to a fuller display.

  2. Puruṣaḥ - ‘pālanāt puruṣaḥ’ (from the root ‘pṛ’ itself, in the sense of ‘pālana’ or protection). The explanation would then be: “bhagavantaṁ pālakaṁ, arthāt rakṣakaṁ karoti iti puruṣakāraḥ”. Lakṣmī makes the Lord ’the protector of the jīvas’.

[[P97]] 84

  1. Puruṣaḥ - ‘puru-bahu, sunoti-dadāti iti puruṣaḥ’. The interpretation, then is: ‘bhagavantaṁ bahuphala-pradaṁ karoti iti puruṣkāraḥ’. Lakṣmī makes the Lord confer many a boon on the jīvas.

These three definitions point to the Lord as ‘Puruṣa’ who is made by Lakṣmī to display in a full measure, his qualities of mercy, protection and generosity.

The following definition is based on the interpretation of the word ‘Puruṣa’ as the jīva (individual soul).

  1. Puruṣaḥ - jīvaḥ (from the root ‘pura’ = agragamane). The etymology is: ‘puruṣaṁ (jīvan) agragāminaṁ karoti iti puruṣakāraḥ’ Lakṣmī, by her timely intercession and proper advice, makes the jīva turn towards the Lord for his protection and forgiveness, and thus helps him. This meaning is made possible since ‘pura’ means ‘going or marching ahead’. To explain, “bhagavad-āśrayaṇavimukhaṁ jīvaṁ bhagavad-agragāminaṁ, bhagavadunmukhaṁ karoti”.

[[P98]] 85

Śrī Embār Jeer of Śrīperumbudur, in his Arumbada-vilakkam on the Śrīvacanabhūṣaṇa, gives another etymology for the word ‘Puruṣakāra’:

“Puruṣau = jīvātma-paramātmānau parasparalābhena sattāvantau karoti iti puruṣakāraḥ lakṣmīḥ”.

Lakṣmī is called the ‘Puruṣakāra’ because she makes the Supreme Brahman and the jīva attain their respective existences. In other words, the Supreme Being becomes similar to an insentient entity unless He attains the individual self (jīva). Likewise, the jīva also becomes similar to a non-entity unless he reaches the Supreme Being. To put it in Sanskrit -

‘paramātmalābhaṁ vinā jīvātmā asat-samaḥ; jīvātmalābhaṁ vinā paramātmapi acit-samaḥ’.

Śrī Tirumaḻiśai Appāppaṅgār Svāmī points out that the word ‘Puruṣakāra’ can afford manifold meanings, as in the case of the sacred mantra, ‘Oṁ Namo Nārāyaṇāya’, where the members ‘a’, ‘ma’, ‘nārāyaṇa’, etc., are interpreted in more than one way. He says -

“akāra - makāra - Nārāyaṇa - Śrīsabdādigaḷaippole puruṣakāraśabdamum anekārthaparam”.

[[P99]] 86

Keeping in mind her role as ‘Puruṣakāra’, the term ‘Śrī’ is also explained in different ways in the Śrīvaiṣṇava tradition. The following verse in the Ahirbudhnya Saṁhitā (LI bI-62a) sums up all these interpretations:

शृणाति निखिलाऩ् दोषाऩ् शृणाति च गुणैर्जगत्। श्रीयते चाखिलैर्नित्यं श्रयते च परं पदम्।। श्रयन्तीं श्रीयमाणां च शृण्वतीं शृण्वतीमपि।। (XXI - 8)

Śrī is so called because:

  1. She is the one who is resorted to by the erring living beings (śrīyate cetanair iti);
  2. She is the one who herself resorts to the Supreme Lord (śrayate bhagavantam iti);
  3. She is the one who listens to the appeals of those who seek refuge under her (śṛṇoti āśrita-vijñāpanam iti);
  4. She is the one who counsels the jīvas who are averse to God (śrāvayati vimukhān iti), or She is the one who makes the Lord listen to the appeals of the erring souls who have resorted to her (śrāvayati bhagavantaṁ svāśrita-vijñāpanam iti);

[[P100]] 87

  1. She is the one who removes or destroys (lit. ‘cooks’) the offences of those who resort to Her (śṛṇāti = hinasti/pacati āśritadoṣān iti); and
  2. She is the one who makes those who resort to her, increase or prosper through their virtues (śṛṇāti = āśritān guṇair vistārayati vardhayati iti).

[[P101]] 88

NĀRĀYAṆA MUNI VS VEDĀNTA RĀMĀNUJA

DIFFERENCES BETWEEN NĀRĀYAṆA MUNI AND VEDĀNTA RĀMĀNUJA

Having studied the text of PM in detail it is worthwhile to note the main differences between Nārāyaṇa Muni and his chief critic Vedānta Rāmānuja Muni in a codified manner in this chapter.

Our understanding of the text of PM is mainly based upon the Maṇidīpikā of ŚŚ, who, as pointed out earlier, must have been the direct disciple of NM. Scholars are of the opinion that the first five pontiffs of the Ahobila Maṭha could have been subscribers to the views of Piḷḷai Lokācārya on the essential nature and role of Lakṣmī.144 The criticism of VR against NM could have been mainly based upon this conception that what NM was trying to explain in his PM was more in keeping with his Teṅgalai tradition than with the Vaḍagalai tradition represented by Vedānta Deśika.

विश्वास-टिप्पनी

While there may be some hair-splitting disagreements with PM along the way, it wouldn’t be credible that STS author should attribute absurd positions to PM.

NM in the very opening verse of PM, may be said to have summarised the central theme of his work.

स्वतन्त्रः स्वेच्छया सृष्टि-
स्थितिस-ंहार-मोक्षणे। यत्-सङ्गं क्रीडतीशस्
तां भजे लोकमातरम्।। 1।। +++(5)+++

[[P102]] 89

According to NM, creation, maintenance, dissolution and liberation of the Universe are the functions of the Lord who is the only independent principle. All these activities take place due to His own free will. He does all these in the presence of the Divine Mother Lakṣmī, which activity becomes their sport. A number of ideas can be deduced from this simple verse:

(1) Viṣṇu and Lakṣmī form the Divine Couple. The Lord alone is responsible for full-fledged creation, dissolution etc.

(2) The role of Lakṣmī can be appreciated as the Mother of the Universe, since she is the consort of the Lord. She is not directly connected with all those cosmic functions, which the Lord performs.

The commentary of ŚŚ brings out the subtleties of this view and explains that Lakṣmī can never have any activity involving or even implying nigraha. The subsequent verse:

स्वयं व्यक्तं रङ्ग-धाम्नि तल्पे वातूल-तूलके।
निवसन्तौ नमाम्याद्यौ दम्पती जनकौ विधेः।। 2।।

qualifies the meaning of the first verse by declaring that this Divine Couple (identified with Lord Raṅganātha and

[[P103]] 90

Raṅganāyakī at Śrīraṅgam) form the parents of Brahmā the four-faced creator God. This verse points out that jagajjanakatva (being parents of the universe) need not be taken in a secondary sense as pitṛtva. It could even mean being the creators directly as in the case of Brahmā who is accepted on all hands as the son of this Divine Couple.

When these two verses are read together it becomes clear that Lakṣmī, the Divine Mother could have been the direct parent of the Brahmā in the primary sense and Mother for the rest of the universe in a secondary sense.

The works of VD speak of Lakṣmī as an attribute of the Lord since she is His ‘patnī’. The secondary status of the ‘patnī’ cannot be denied, contends NM. There are several instances in the scriptural passages which posit similarity between the Lord and His consort. There are also passages speaking of utmost similarity (atyanta-tulyatā) between them.

The chief purpose of PM therefore, is to decide beyond doubt if Lakṣmī the Patnī can lay claims to all the features of Her Lord, in the manner He possesses them ‘patnyāḥ pativad īdrktvam asti neti nirūpyate’ (PM. p.6).

Vedānta Rāmānuja Muni whose ŚTS was ‘designed chiefly to demolish’ the PM, takes exception to the stand taken by NM on one important issue namely Her Upāyatva.

[[P104]] 91

According to NM, Lord alone is the direct means of salvation but not Lakṣmī. Lakṣmī’s being the upāya for Mokṣa is also acknowledged in some scriptural and Āgama passages and openly expressed in the stotras of Ācāryas as well. But NM prefers to explain this upāyatva through Lakṣmī’s status as an ‘attribute’ of the Lord and never as the substantive, that is the Lord.

Regarding nigraha also, while VR points out sāmarthya (capacity) to punish the wicked as being present in the Divine Mother, NM contends that even granting this, Lakṣmī never desires to display it.

“śaktiḥ śriyo’sti neccheti” (Kārikā 41a)

For NM the Viśeṣaṇatva of Lakṣmī is the key which unlocks the flood-gates of a number of features such as kāraṇatva, upāsyatva, upāyatva and prāpyatva. Her creation is marked by pure and unalloyed grace. She receives the Bhara, and confers upon the devotees supreme Bliss through sheer love and affection. The Lord is a daṇḍadhara but Lakṣmī is entirely devoid of this quality.

In so far as conferring Mokṣa is concerned while VR contends that Lakṣmī is as powerful and full-fledged an upāya as the Lord is, NM makes her the upāya through the

[[P105]] 92

golden means of Her status as an Attribute. The passage ‘kāraṇatvādi na śriyaḥ’ shows that the kind of kāraṇatva mentioned of Brahman in the Śrutis and Brahmasūtra is not found in Lakṣmī. It does not deprive Lakṣmī of Her glory or status. The Lord is all the time qualified by Lakṣmī. Therefore whatever functions the Lord, has Lakṣmī also can share in. One cannot imagine a substantive without an attribute. Whatever feature the substantive possesses can also be ascribed to the Viśeṣaṇa which is a part and parcel of the substantive.

Lakṣmī’s role as jagatkāraṇa, as intended by Vedānta Deśika in his NS and other works, has been fully subscribed to by NM in his PM. Deśika’s CŚB speaks of the relationship of Lakṣmī with Her Lord in terms of svāmitva, saulabhya, phaladatva and phalatva. The word phaladatva means upāyatva. That Lakṣmī also becomes an upāya through Her status as Lord’s consort is acceptable to Deśika himself, contends NM.

Lakṣmī can also confer Mokṣa, but not in the way Her husband does. The Lord confers Mokṣa only after giving up His wrath. But in the case of Lakṣmī since she is incapable of getting angry, Her conferring Mokṣa will be through Her pure grace alone.145

[[P106]] 93

According to NM, Lakṣmī being the attribute of the Lord becomes the soul of the entire universe which forms Her body. She becomes a śeṣiṇī, she forms the kartrī, niyantrī, the source of all Bliss and the chief object of meditation like Her Lord. She is all-pervasive and also the ruler like the Lord. But she is still subordinate to the Lord by mutual will and understanding. VR’s criticism that NM makes Lakṣmī equal to the jīvas is quite unfounded. The definition given in the NS to Īśvaratva, is ‘svajñāna-svetara-dravya-śarīrakatvam’ (‘possessing everything other than Himself and the knowledge as His body’). The characteristics of the jīva‘are said to be eight in number, viz., ādheyatva, vidheyatva, śeṣatva and aṇutva each of which is to be taken to qualify cetanatvam and ahantvaṁ severally. The characteristic of the Lord are four-fold viz., ‘mumukṣūpāsyatva; mokṣapradatva; prāpyatva and ananyādhāratva’.

According to NM Lakṣmī can never be similar to a jīva. Lakṣmī is coeval with the Lord in all His aspects excepting in Her having nigraha. There is sāmya between both of them but not in so far as nigraha and its effects are concerned.146

[[P107]] 94

According to NM the definition of Īśvara found in the NS has nothing to do with Lakṣmī’s nature. It is meant to preclude Brahmā, Indra and other gods from the scope of the definition. According to VR’s charge NM should agree that Lakṣmī also being the body of the Lord becomes equal to a jīva, in which case he cannot claim any special status for Her. If Lakṣmī’s sāmya with the Lord is accepted, she being co-eval with Him in all His aspects, she too will be included in the definition of Īśvara.

In so far as Her svarūpa is concerned, Lakṣmī according to NM is pāratantra (dependent on the Lord). This pāratantrya is subjected to the will of both. In the case of jīvas however, it is purely dependent on the will of the Lord. Therefore Lakṣmī can never be a jīva, since she lacks in svātantrya and nigraha. According to the true and full implication of Bṛhattva, from the viewpoint of svarūpa and guṇa, she cannot be the connotation of the term Brahman, points out NM. This clearly defines the position of NM regarding the nature and status of Lakṣmī. Total similarity between them in all aspects is what VR stresses which has its own limitations according to NM, as explained by ŚŚ. Lakṣmī’s

[[P108]] 95

‘independence’ is marked by Her ‘dependence on the Lord’s will’. According to NM, Deśika’s Gadya Bhāṣya and Tattvatīkā make this point clear.147

NM repeatedly refers to the fact that Lakṣmī becomes the ruler of the Universe only on the ground of having both the Vibhūtis under Her control. In this she is on par with the Lord.148 But regarding hetutva, upāsyatva etc., Lord alone possesses them but Lakṣmī can also lay claim to them through Her status as an attribute of the Lord. Even forming the object of meditation (upāsyatva) is different in the case of Lakṣmī. One prays to the Lord alone for having the experience of complete Bliss. Lakṣmī also may enter the picture only as an attribute of the Brahman because she, as a Puruṣakāra, helps to remove the nigraha of the Lord and thus can find a place there also. She does not form the direct object of meditation.

The main reason for controversies regarding the nature and status of Lakṣmī can be traced to various

[[P109]] 96

scriptural passages and the varying statements of the ācāryas. Some texts speak of her sāmya with the Lord. Others refer to their aikya; others refer to Lakṣmī as the śakti of ahantā or tadvattā. Deśika has tried to interpret all these passages in a very synthetic and pragmatic manner. The golden principle of dāmpatya between Śrī and Viṣṇu is the thesis developed by Deśika. With this principle of dāmpatya, everything can explained satisfactorily. Tadvattā or śaktitva ultimately means Viśeṣaṇatva, according to NM.

Though a Viśeṣaṇa of the Lord, Lakṣmī according to NM has her own essential difference from the Lord (svarūpa-bheda) as in the case of the beams and the Moon. Yāmuna’s statement ‘kāntāste’ using the sixth case (in ते) really brings out the difference between Lakṣmī and the Lord and in fact this is the reflection of the śruti-passage ‘hrīśca te lakṣmīśca patnyau’ (Taittirīya Āraṇyaka 3-13-2).

According to NM, the Supreme Brahman qualified by Śrī alone is the object of prapatti. The definition of149

[[P110]] 97

prapatti ‘ananya-sādhye’ etc., the mantra which speaks of it viz., the Dvaya and the Caramaśloka which ordains it, several Āgama texts, and the Śrī Bhāṣya of Rāmānuja and the tradition are in favour of status of Lakṣmī as a Viśeṣaṇa. She can never become an upalakṣaṇa as alleged by others. Lakṣmī and the Lord both become the recipients of ‘ātmahavis’ in the context of what is known as ‘avanayajña’. The Lord is the Yajamāna and Lakṣmī being His patnī also receives this Havis. This clearly states that Lakṣmī becomes an attribute alone like other guṇas and vigraha of the Lord.150

Lakṣmī’s upayoga in the ‘sacrifice of protection’ lies in generating a steady love and concentration towards Him in his devotees. She does things favourable to the Lord by giving consent to His protective function. She removes the unapproachability, ‘ādhṛṣyatva’ of the Lord by Her very presence. Even during the stage of Nyāsa she remains an attribute of the Lord; she destroys the sins of devotees, generates a taste for the Lord who is the goal, and ensures His grace for them. All this is the implication of Her Puruṣa-kāratva alone.151

[[P111]] 98

According to NM and VR Lakṣmī forms the Puruṣakāra also. They both agree that there is as sāmarthya in her. But VR tries relate this sāmarthya to kriyā, and thus, make Lakṣmī the sahakartrī in the act of protection. This according to him is the upāyatva. But according to NM as explained by ŚŚ, sāmarthya must necessarily involve kriyā, which in the case of Lakṣmī is not possible. In other words she cannot do things directly involving nigraha as the Lord does.

Therefore there is between them what is called aikarasya which means sāmarasya. It is this ‘identity of tastes’ that makes Lakṣmī indirectly, a component in the scheme of upāya.

Thus the main difference between NM and VR lies in establishing Lakṣmī’s upāyatva through sāmarasya and not merely through sāmarthya. Even her role as Puruṣakāra becomes fruitful only through sāmarasya.152

As a Viśeṣaṇa of the Lord she becomes the kāraṇa also, of course indirectly. She is different from gods like Brahmā and Indra who in the Pratardanavidyā form the viśeṣaṇas of the Lord. This is the difference between NM and VR: Though dependent on the Lord, Lakṣmī can grant Mokṣa also by granting sāmya etc.

[[P112]] 99

NM is of the opinion that the excellence of Lakṣmī strictly speaking, is dependent upon the Lord and therefore, it is not natural to her (’svatassiddhā’). But this guṇabhāva is the result of mutual will, (ubhayecchā). Still this does not undermine her greatness.

According to NM Lakṣmī cannot be the means of liberation ‘after shedding anger’ (kopanivṛttipūrvaka) because this is a feature unique with the Lord only. When a substantive which is qualified is totally negated the intention is to negate the attribute only.

VR charges NM for equating Lakṣmī with other pāratantra-jīvas, and making her devoid of subāśrayatva, by denying her the powers to grant Mokṣa. But according to NM she does not have the desire to confer mokṣa like the Lord. Lakṣmī is the abode of all auspiciousness according to NM also. Her upāyatva lies in her bestowing the experience of complete bliss on the jīvas but the upāyatva of the Lord lies in His conferring such an experience after shedding His wrath. Duality of upāyas is not acceptable to NM either. The relation of Lakṣmī with the Lord is comparable to the one between a gem and its radiance, flower and its fragrance, the Moon and her

[[P113]] 100

beams, nectar and its sweetness. This is natural but not adventitious. Śrī is an apṛthaksiddha-dharma of the Lord. Her relation with Him is ‘yāvadātmabhāvī’ (as long as she exists), which means ’eternal’.

Lakṣmī removes or destroys all the doṣas in those who surrender and this helps the blooming of the upāya to its fulness. As explained by ŚŚ under the kārikā the special destination of the PM lies in the fact that Lakṣmī has been explained as an upāya through her status as viśeṣaṇa but not as the upāya directly, as held by VR. This is acceptable to VD as understood from RTS and NT. Kumāravarada in his commentary on NT has also explained Lakṣmī’s status as an attribute on the analogy of certain Vedic expressions like ‘mahendra’, and ‘agniṣoma’153 involving Dvandva Compound. The same point is also emphasised under the sūtra, ‘vṛddhihrāsa’ etc. (Brahma-sūtra: 3-2-20) as explained by Rāmānuja.

Another difference between NM and VR is regarding the implication of the word dampati. According to VR, it indicates equal status between both husband and wife

इशिता शौनह्यान्ता घटकोपेश रक्षितः।। [K 104 ]

[[P114]] 101

(samaprādhānya). But for NM, who quotes Varadācārya’s commentary of NT, relatively Lord is more important. Several sections of the RTS also indicate this. Because she is a viśeṣaṇa to the Lord, she has lesser importance than the Lord. Equal importance is not possible. Whatever kind of prapatti one may do to the Lord, svarūpa, bhara or phala, she remains only a viśeṣaṇa to the Lord.154 Even in yantras(motifs) dedicated to Lakṣmī, the overall importance of Lakṣmī cannot be accepted, the Lord being the innermost controller of Lakṣmī also. He becomes the uddeśya of worship here too.

The salient features of PM are found in the commentary of ŚŚ towards the end of the text. Lakṣmī is the direct agent in all the cosmic activities involving anugraha. But in activities involving nigraha which is the special prerogative of the Lord, she becomes only a prompting agent. She is also the inner controller of all the beings. She is also the ādhāra of all, of course expecting the Lord. Her control (niyamana) of the living beings is155

विशेषणं शरव्यस्य भर्जन्यस् तथ्यापि था।। K110।।

[[P115]] 102

through pure love and motherly affection. She becomes the mistress of the Universe (śeṣiṇī) quite naturally but not as a result of any adventitious condition. She is all-pervasive and forms the recipient of ātmahavis. She functions as the Puruṣakāra, becoming the viśeṣaṇa of the Lord. Like the Lord she too has Cit and Acit as Her body. She is the mother of the entire creation and as a result of mutual will between herself and the Lord, she becomes the śeṣā, niyāmyā, pāratantrā and ādheyā in relation to the Lord. Another special point which NM stresses is that she is not a mere bestower of wealth (dhanadā) as held by some. Towards the end of the text NM stresses that as outlined by Deśika in his Catuśślokī-bhāṣya both in the opening and concluding portions, Lakṣmī is always associated with the Lord and thereby removes the fear of those who want to approach Him. If the Lord is the Svāmī, she becomes the Svāminī. She is sulabhā, phaladā and the phala itself purely by her association with the Lord as an attribute.

We may therefore conclude that the points of difference between NM and VR are only limited. All these differences boil down to upāyatva only, which

[[P116]] 103

is the main point of contention between VR and NM. The kāraṇatva of Lakṣmī is also a moot point. So is her viśeṣaṇatva. NM argues that by virtue of Her viśeṣaṇatva only Lakṣmī can be justified as the upāya, upeya, kāraṇa, Puruṣakāra, Īśvarī and so on. This concept of viśeṣaṇatva has been there in the very nature of Lakṣmī, scriptures confirm it and tradition allows it. That she is the patnī of the Lord makes her automatically subordinate to Him as the co-performer of his duties. This only adds to the excellence of Śrī and the Lord, because both of them,by mutual will, have become the couple. A comparative study of these two works of the ācāryas viz., the PM and ŚTS inspite of their apparent controversies and contradictions, is a rewarding experience in itself as it highlights several subtle points of the tradition which have their own place and value.

[[P117]] 104

DETAILED ANALYSIS

DETAILED ANALYSIS OF THE PURUṢAKĀRA MĪMĀṀSĀ WITH THE COMMENTARY MAṆIDĪPIKĀ

The Puruṣakāra-mīmāṁsā (PM) of Nārāyaṇa Muni, has a lucid commentary Maṇidīpikā by Śrīśaileśa (ŚŚ) which helps in understanding the intricacies of the concept of Śrī as Puruṣakāra. ŚŚ explains each and every word of the śloka providing scriptural evidences such as those from Vedas, Upaniṣads, the Rāmāyaṇa, Mahābhārata, Viṣṇupurāṇa etc. He also provides supporting passages from the works of earlier ācāryas, like Yāmuna, Rāmānuja Kūreśvara, Parāśara Bhaṭṭa and Vedānta Deśika. The bulk of his quotations is from the Catuśślokī with Deśika’s commentary.

After paying obeisance to Lord Kuranganātha the presiding deity at Thirukkuruṅguḍi and His consort, Viṣvaksena and Nammāḻvār, Śrīśaileśa mentions Śrī Rāmānuja, Varada Viṣṇvārya and Vedānta Deśika as the ācāryas who established the Viśiṣṭādvaita tradition. Then he refers to his own father Vātsya Rājagopāla at whose feet he learnt about the real nature of Lakṣmī and Her consort. He also refers to one Ammāḷārya as his teacher. Then he refers to Śrīmannārāyaṇa Muni

[[P118]] 106

all that the Lord performs, including destruction. But since she is purely of the nature of Anugraha (compassion) and also since the scriptures state that Bhagavān alone is the daṇḍadhara (chastiser), Lakṣmī can never be directly connected with activities involving nigraha; she can only indirectly be related to such activities. But there is nothing objectionable in her being directly connected with activities involving anugraha.

ŚŚ then moves on to the next verse, ‘Svayam vyakte’.156 This is also by way of paying obeisance to the Divine Couple abiding in Śrīraṅgam on the serpent couch.

ŚŚ then takes up the verse ‘Śrípatiḥ’ etc.157 He does not comment upon the following verse which is a prayer to Viṣvaksena, the consort of Sūtravatī, who creates sustains and destroys the universe by his mere Saṅkalpa, and who puts off all impediments, by the vibrations of his Vetra.

सङ्कल्पेनैव यो विश्वं सृजत्यवति हन्ति यः। वेत्रस्पन्दास्तविधिं तं वन्दे सूत्रवतीश्वम्।। (v. 3.)

निवसन्तो नमाम्याद्यौ दम्पती जनको विधेः।। (v. 2.)

[[P119]] 106

all that the Lord performs, including destruction. But since she is purely of the nature of Anugraha (compassion) and also since the scriptures state that Bhagavān alone is the daṇḍadhara (chastiser), Lakṣmī can never be directly connected with activities involving nigraha; she can only indirectly be related to such activities. But there is nothing objectionable in her being directly connected with activities involving anugraha.

ŚŚ then moves on to the next verse, ‘Svayam vyakte’.158 This is also by way of paying obeisance to the Divine Couple abiding in Śrīraṅgam on the serpent couch.

ŚŚ then takes up the verse ‘Śrípatiḥ’ etc.159 He does not comment upon the following verse which is a prayer to Viṣvaksena, the consort of Sūtravatī, who creates sustains and destroys the universe by his mere Saṅkalpa, and who puts off all impediments, by the vibrations of his Vetra.

सङ्कल्पेनैव यो विश्वं सृजत्यवति हन्ति यः। वेत्रस्पन्दास्तविधिं तं वन्दे सूत्रवतीश्वम्।। (v. 3.)

निवसन्तो नमाम्याद्यौ दम्पती जनको विधेः।। (v. 2.)

[[P120]] 107

Commenting on Kārikā, ‘Śrīpatiḥ’ etc., ŚŚ observes that Lord Viṣṇu alone, to the exclusion of all others independently confers Mokṣa, when resorted to by those who are desirous of it. But doubts have been raised by some people regarding the exact nature and powers of Śrī because, in the works of the earlier ācāryas are found statements that Lakṣmī also, like the Lord is the ruler of all and that there is therefore, sāmya (similarity) between them. There are others who state that there is utmost identity (atyanta-tulyatā) between the Lord and Lakṣmī on several issues such as causality of the entire universe, being the refuge of all, and conferment of Mokṣa. Some others are however of the view that utmost similarity cannot be the meaning of expressions like Sarveśvaratva (being the ruler of all) because there are innumerable āgama-texts and also the declarations of Śrī Vedānta Deśika to the effect that Lakṣmī happens to be the patnī and an attribute (viśeṣaṇa) of the Lord, and also that she is the Mother and Puruṣakāra of all living beings. Therefore atyanta-sāmya must be understood in a slightly narrower sense, they argue. Because of these controversial view-points Nārāyaṇa Muni (NM) undertook to compose the Puruṣakāra Mīmāṁsā with a view to clear all doubts and establish the true nature

[[P121]] 108

of Lakṣmī according to the highest traditions of Viśiṣṭādvaita Vedānta. Thus he states ‘patnyāḥ pativadīdrktvamasti neti nirūpyate’. So the real concern of this work is to examine whether or not Lakṣmī also becomes an independent cause like the Lord, and also to find out if she becomes a means of liberation and the recipient of śaraṇāgati like Him.

The Pūrvapakṣa-view raised by NM is that Lakṣmī also is the Cause of the universe, the person to be resorted to and the bestower of Mokṣa directly since there are scriptural statements that she is equal to the Lord in all respects. These Pūrvapakṣins attribute this view to Vedānta Deśika himself, but NM points out that the Siddhānta-view entertained by Vedānta Deśika is that the Lord alone is the cause of the Universe and that He has to be resorted to for liberation; that He becomes the protector and the goal to be attained along with Lakṣmī (śriyā sārdham). ŚŚ points out that all pramāṇas and established tradition are unanimous that Lakṣmī exists for the sake of the Lord for eternity (nityasiddha-patipāratantrya). She is the Mother and hence Her nature is of the very essence of anugraha or mercy. Therefore there

[[P122]] 109

is nothing wrong in Her being construed as the cause of the universe,the object of refuge and the bestower of Mokṣa, like the Lord. She is also the goal of human endeavour like Him. She is incapable of being hard-hearted (nighrahabhāva) and so, all the contingencies of ‘strictness’ such as creation of different kinds of hells,various types of punishments therein, etc., do not arise in her case. Therefore, strictly speaking, she cannot be called the cause of the universe ‘in its entirety’ (nikhila). It is for this very reason (i.e. since she cannot get angry) she cannot also be the recipient of bhara-samarpaṇa which is marked by the absence of strictness although she becomes the recipient of bhara-samarpaṇa characterised by pure grace. Therefore this kind of upāyatva, i.e., conferring the fruit after ‘giving up the strictness’ (nigraha-nivṛtti-ghaṭita) also becomes absurd in the case of Lakṣmī. She becomes the goal (prāpya)by becoming the recipient of different kinds of Kaiṅkarya rendered by the different souls. There is no question of nigraha at all in her and there is total similarity between her and the Lord on this issue of being the recipients of Kaiṅkarya. This is the final settled opinion of the Siddhāntin, says ŚŚ. The point to be kept in mind is that creating, sustaining, dissolving and emancipating the cosmos

[[P123]] 110

in toto naturally involves a tendency to be strict and hard-hearted, readiness to punish the evil-doers (nigraha), if necessary. All these certainly become the characteristics of the Supreme Brahman but not Lakṣmī. This is the quintessential point on which the present text is based, points out Śrīśaileśa.

Introducing the next verse which discusses the role of Lakṣmī regarding creation etc of the universe, ŚŚ brings in the view entertained by Vedānta Rāmānuja (VR) in his Śrītattva Siddhāñjana (ŚTS).160 According to ŚTS the Lord’s essential nature, which is peculiar to Himself, is marked by the ṣāḍguṇya, five aspects (para, vyūha, etc.) and creation, maintenance, dissolution and emancipation of all the worlds. These must be held to be common in the case of Lakṣmī also; or otherwise, Lakṣmī can never be held to be equal to the Lord, as declared by the śrutis. VR draws a line between the characteristics of Īśvara and those of the Brahman. Īśvaratva is marked by the mere presence of the capacity (sāmarthya-mātra) to create the entire universe, sustain it, etc. As contrasted with this the characteristics of the Brahman are the possession of

[[P124]] 111

spontaneous and natural capacity (akṛtaka-sāmarthya) and the actual display of that capacity in action. If there is a cosmic function, then it becomes the characteristic of the Brahman. Such a thing is absent in the liberated and ever-liberated souls as understood, which is declared by the Brahmasūtra, ‘jagadvyāpāravarjam’ etc (IV.4.17). This is what Vedānta Deśika has stated in his commentary on Śrī Rāmānuja’s Śrīvaikuṇṭhagadya also.161 The Brahmasūtra ‘janmādyasya yataḥ’ (I.1.2) focuses itself on the Brahmalakṣaṇa, namely, the entire activity (Kṛtsna-vyāpāra)concerning creation etc., of the universe. The word kṛtsna must qualify the word Vyāpāra so as to exclude the over-pervasion of the definition to the four-faced Brahmā and others,who are also creators in a sense but not creators of everything, like the Lord. According to ŚTS, the Vyāpāras in toto include also daṇḍadharatva (being a chastiser), which is totally absent from Lakṣmī. The entirety of cosmic activity includes creation of those who live in hells (nārakins), their maintenance and their individual destruction, which activity can never be traced to Lakṣmī. The chief point of VR is that all cosmic activities such as creation, maintenance, dissolution and

[[P125]] 112

liberation must be held to be common to both the Lord and His consort. But the distinction between the two lies in the latter (Lakṣmī) being free from the creation, maintenance and dissolution of the inmates of various types of hells.

ŚŚ then introduces the next Kārikā of the text ‘antaḥ praviśya’ etc.,162 which proves beyond doubt that the Lord becomes the creator of everything through His Saṅkalpa to become ‘many’, who controls everything from within, forming its soul. The commentator adds that all the Vedāntas such as ‘sadeva somya’ ’tadaikṣata’ and ‘so’kāmayata’ point to this. Lakṣmī however cannot be such a cause because (1) she cannot afford to be a punisher; (2) she cannot dispense with justice according to the karman of the living beings assuming nigraha and anugraha as the case may be,and (3) she has nothing to do with the creation of hell etc. She can never be the controller (niyantṛtva) looking after or regulating the cosmic activities in their entirety.

ŚŚ then comments upon the next Kārikā, ‘Kāraṇatva-prakaraṇa’etc.,163 examining the status of Lakṣmī’s causality

[[P126]] 113

more minutely. The prima facie view raised is that the presence of Lakṣmī is indicated at the time of creation by such words as ‘śraddhā’ and ‘svadhā’. The text ‘Āsyesanā’ etc., makes it clear that Lakṣmī becomes the controller of all (niyantṛtva) which again leads to her being soul of all (as the antyaryāminī). Therefore having everything in common with the Lord, Lakṣmī can be accepted as the cause of the entire universe. It is in refutation of this that the Kārikā, ‘Kāraṇatvaprakaraṇe’ is introduced by NM. NM opines that Lakṣmī’s presence has nowhere been indicated in the context whereas the Lord alone is spoken of as the cause of the universe. Further nowhere is she said to have cit and acit as Her body, or stated to be controlling everything from within, as the Lord is. The word ‘pativat’ has to be read into the verse to make the sense complete, says ŚŚ, because the discussion had earlier been opened with the statement ‘patnyāṁ, pativadīdrktvam asti neti nirūpyate’ (We are going to discuss whether this kind of similarity between Her Lord and Her consort, actually exists or not).164

[[P127]] 114

Explaining, ŚŚ observes that the words Śraddhā, Svadhā etc., certainly refer to the presence of Lakṣmī but there is no speciality attached to it. In other words Lakṣmī has no direct bearing on personal involvement in the actual creation of the universe like the Lord. The passage “śraddhayā devo devatvamaśnute” (Yaj.Kāṭ. 3-9-12) has been explained by Vedānta Deśika in his Catuśślokī Bhāṣya as suggesting the presence of Lakṣmī as a mere attribute to the Lord, merely keeping company with Him and that it is not of any significance (prādhānya) in so far as the actual creation etc., are concerned. Further, ācāryas like Kūreśa and Parāśara state that the Lord creates the universe as a sportive gesture to please His consort165 and that she approves of His activities by Her mere glances.166 167

The central idea is this: The Supreme Being has been stated to be the all-soul and all-controller in texts like the Antaryāmī Brāhmaṇa. Depending upon the good and bad deeds performed by the jīva-s, he controls them

[[P128]] from within, through nigraha and anugraha. Śrī who is His attribute (Viśeṣaṇa) also abides within the jīvas as their inner controller and in accordance with their sukṛta (good deeds) directs them and engages herself in this kind of niyamaṇa which is motivated by pure grace. But never does she control them through nigraha. There again, it must be understood that she has the power to show nigraha, but she never has a desire to display it.168 This has to be accepted on the authority of scriptures which speak of Lakṣmī as an embodiment of anugraha characterised by motherhood and mediacy. Śrī Deśika while interpreting the word Svadhā does not seem to favour the presence of Lakṣmī in the context of causality. Still, while explaining the text ‘Anīdavātam’, he first makes out that the Brahman does not depend upon anybody for His existence. Subsequently however, he interprets that Lakṣmī’s presence is also to be accepted (sahayoga). He concludes, on the basis of a quotation from the Rāmāyaṇa that the Lord may be said to depend upon His consort (Svadhā) in the sense that He has so much of love for Her. There is no room however to suspect that Lakṣmī thereby becomes the cause of the universe like Her Lord.

[[P129]] 116

The succeeding Kārikā ‘yatsaṅkalpāt’169 according to ŚŚ, brings out the role of Lakṣmī as a mere Viśeṣaṇa of the Lord who alone is the creator of this universe by His mere saṅkalpa and who alone forms the single object of meditation. In all the aspects of the Lord - Kāraṇatva, Upāsyatva, Upāyatva and prāpyatva, Śrī becomes His attribute. Her specific function or utility in being the Viśeṣaṇa lies in Her bringing out creation etc., involving pure Grace, in receiving the bhara (responsibility) of those who surrender to Her, for the full benefit of experiencing Mokṣa) and also in conferring upon them that kind of experience through sheer love and affection. It is necessary here to draw a line between the functions of Lord and those of Lakṣmī because, the Lord alone is known as daṇḍadhara. Śrī Deśika in the verse ‘yatsaṅkalpāt’ etc., of his Śrīstuti (no. 4) expresses the same idea.

In all such cases, Lakṣmī must be understood to be included in the personality of the Lord although Her presence is not expressly stated.170

Śrīśaileśa refers to an opinion expressed by scholars, that the presence of Lakṣmī is absolutely

[[P130]] 117

absent in the context of causality, because the Kārikā quoted earlier’kāraṇatvaprakaraṇe’ etc., itself declares to that effect. ŚŚ answers that the intention of the passage is different. It merely states that Lakṣmī does not appear in that context as an important functionary involving herself personally in the creative activity along with the Lord. The sahānvaya of Lakṣmī has to be clearly understood, he warns.

ŚŚ in this context also refutes another view that the Sahānvaya of Lakṣmī in the context of causality merely refers to Her sāmarthya (capacity). The word sāmarthya suggesting (eligibility) cannot convey the complete idea that Lakṣmī can do all that the Lord actually does.

Deśika in his Tattvatīkā states that conferring Mokṣa is an exclusive characteristic of the Brahman. If that be so, how can this power be stated to exist in both Lord and His consort? This question is answered on the ground that although both are accepted as the cause of the Universe, performing all the activities regarding creation etc., in toto alone characterises Brahman. On the same analogy, conferring Mokṣa also can be attributed to both although it is the exclusive

[[P131]] 118

prerogative of Brahman alone. As a matter of fact NM in the PM itself specifies the exact role of Lakṣmī as the Viśeṣaṇa of the Lord.171

Although Lakṣmī is the Viśeṣaṇa, she can still be construed as being ‘related’ to the cosmic activities. Śrīśaileśa, introducing the succeeding two Kārikās172 observes that the definition of the term ‘Brahman’ should involve all the cosmic functions, in all their plenitude. Śrī Deśika in his Tattvatīkā173 mentions six characteristics of Brahman, namely, that He is the cause of everything that is created; that He is the object of meditation for those who seek liberation; that He is the one who confers Mokṣa; that He is the chief import of all Vedāntas; that He is the consort of Śrī and that He is the ultimate goal. The statement that ‘kāraṇatvādi na śriyaḥ’ merely intends to state that the Kāraṇatva mentioned of Brahman as stated above, and as corroborated in the Śrutis and Brahmasūtra is not to be found in the case of Lakṣmī. It does not

[[P132]] 119

preclude the presence of Lakṣmī as the Viśeṣaṇa wherever the Lord is mentioned as the kāraṇa, upāsya, upāya and prāpya.

ŚŚ controverts the view of VR that Lakṣmī is not referred to in the Śrutis and Sūtra, although, he does not accept the characteristics of Brahman in Lakṣmī as involving the creation etc.of the entire universe. Posing various alternatives and quoting the Tattvatīkā,the NS, Stotra Bhāṣya etc., of Vedānta Deśika and various Kārikās of the PM, ŚŚ contends that such an opinion cannot be entertained. The Lord is all the time qualified by Lakṣmī and there cannot be a speck of doubt about it.

ŚŚ also examines in this context the allegations made by VR against NM, that he contradicts the opinion of VD who declared that Lakṣmī also is jagatkāraṇa in his NS and other works.

The intention of the passage is entirely different according to ŚŚ. What is meant is, that Lakṣmī is not responsible for all the cosmic activities and that she is incapable of certain functions which the Lord alone is capable of. She has the capacity of carrying on all the cosmic activities but she is not involved in those

[[P133]] 120

activities in full. There is no contradiction involved in the statements of NM. As a matter of fact the Catuśślokī Bhāṣya of Deśika does not speak of all these cosmic activities with reference to Lakṣmī. It merely speaks of the relationship Lakṣmī has with Her consort in terms of svāmitva, saulabhya, phaladatva and phalatva. That she is also the mistress of the universe that she is of easy access, that she confers mokṣa and that she also constitutes the phala in association with Her Lord, is what is meant by these terms.

ŚŚ also clears the misconception that there is mutual contradiction in the statements made by Deśika in his TT and NS. The TT states that the Brahmalakṣaṇa cannot be applied to Lakṣmī and the NS points out that the Divine Couple constitutes the cause of the universe. It is true that there seems to be a contradiction here. But it is only apparent. In the context of TT Deśika merely kept in mind the causality of the universe in all its aspects without bringing out the characteristics of Lakṣmī such as motherhood and grace. But in the NS, those facts have been taken into consideration. So there is no contradiction here.

[[P134]] 121

ŚŚ then moves on to the next Kārikā174 emphasising the point that Lakṣmī is characterised by mātṛtva and anugraha alone and as such, we cannot attribute all cosmic activities to Her. This is what this Kārikā of PM states.

‘If Lakṣmī were to be considered the cause of the creation, destruction, punishment etc.of certain lower orders of beings, such as trees and plants, how can one understand her role as the Mediator (Puruṣakāra) and Mother?’ asks NM.

In the next Kārikā175 NM states that Lakṣmī is not stated in the śrutis, Brahmasūtra, Śrī Bhāṣya, the three Gadyas, Vedāntasāra, in the various stotras of earlier ācāryas and their commentaries as the cause of the Universe on par with Her Lord. Even if there are statements in a few śrutis that Lakṣmī is the kāraṇa, these must be reviewed in the context of Her essential character namely benign grace, and are to be interpreted in a restricted sense.

[[P135]] 122

ŚŚ then takes up the next verse ‘Rahasyatraya-sāradeli’ etc.,176 and explains that a few commentaries in the RTS of Vedānta Deśika, make out a case for Lakṣmī’s being the niyantrī (controller) of the living beings. But, these statements must be clearly analysed, keeping in mind Lakṣmī’s essential nature viz., that she has no strictness (nigraha) in dealing with the living beings. Her cosmic functions including the conferring of Mokṣa must also be carefully understood. E.g., Lakṣmī also confers Mokṣa but not in the way her husband does it. The Lord confers Mokṣa on a person only after giving up His nigraha. That means, He first shows His anger or strictness enforces strict discipline, and only thereafter he sheds anger and confers Mokṣa. But since Lakṣmī is incapable of showing any nigraha, statements that she confers Mokṣa must be understood in a different way. That is, she shows anugraha only and through that, confers Mokṣa. There are therefore such intricacies involved in explaining the role of Lakṣmī in regard to cosmic activities. That is why NM says in the Kārikā ‘sancintyaḥ arthab kvacit kvacit’ (‘The matter has to be,

[[P136]] 123

depending upon the context, reviewed in the proper light.) It has already been pointed out that because Lakṣmī is always associated with Her Lord (sahayoga), Lakṣmī stands as an attribute to the Lord who forms the substantive. She cannot grant Mokṣa or become the kāraṇa of all cosmic activities like the Lord and whatever is understood about Lakṣmī must be essentially streamlined by Her position as the consort of the Lord.

Liberated souls are said to have extreme similarity (paramasāmya) to the Lord. But this has to be understood in a restricted sense only as explained in the Sūtra, ‘jagadvyāpāravarjam’ etc. (IV. 4.17). In the case of Lakṣmī also the same principle has to be adopted. She too is said to be ’extremely similar’ to the Lord. But still she is of a different nature (Cf. Sāttvata Saṁhitā ‘bhinnalakṣaṇam’) That she is the consort (patnī) of the Lord and that she is dependent (paratantra) on Him, are quite well-known. That she is the Mother, full of unmotivated love for the beings and that she acts as a mediator between them and the Lord are also equally well-known. Therefore statements that she is ’totally similar’ to the Lord must be understood within the framework of these accepted features. Texts like the Tattvatīkā make this point clear. The functions of Lakṣmī

[[P137]] 124

in association with her Lord have been clearly brought out by VD in the opening verse of his commentary on the Catuśślokī.177

Summarising the discussion ŚŚ states that although certain qualities are common among the Divine couple, certain qualities are strikingly different – nigraha and its effects are peculiar to the Lord alone and not to Lakṣmī. Therefore His causal character is underlined by His nigraha. This kind of causal character cannot be found in Lakṣmī. Therefore, pointing out a defect in PM’s statement ‘Kāraṇatvādina śriyaḥ’ does not carry weight. Absence of certain qualities in Lakṣmī does not make Her the Brahman technically, but this does not deny Her the status of being equal to Him in other aspects. This is what is going to be stated later on in the Kārikā, ‘śruti-sūtrādisamsiddhaiḥ’ etc.178

ŚŚ then introduces the next Kārikā of PM ‘prapanna pārijāta ca’ etc.179 According to this, Vātsya Varada in

[[P138]] 125

his PP did not mention Lakṣmī as the Kāraṇa although she forms the Viśeṣaṇa of the Lord. But what he stressed is her role as Puruṣakāra, which becomes invariable and essential at the time of Nyāsa. In other words, Lakṣmī’s status as Puruṣakāra becomes significant only when we do Śaraṇāgati to the Lord. ŚŚ quotes the relevant passages of the PP to show that jīvas who are ever prone to commit offences cannot themselves approach the Lord. It is then that Lakṣmī steps in as the Puruṣakāra. Because of her love for the Lord, she easily approaches Him, and increases His affection for the beings at the right moment. His qualities like jñāna and śakti will be heightened by Her because they will be helpful in protecting the jīvas. By Her own personal charm, she will also bring out the charm of the Lord which becomes an object of enjoyment for the devotees. The word ‘jagadīśitrī’ of this quotation may mean that Lakṣmī becomes the ruler (niyantrī), implying Her causal character also. But here again, as pointed earlier, we have to restrict the meaning of Her causality since she is incapable of showing any nigraha.

The next Kārikā, ‘Vṛkṣādi’ etc.,180 has already been referred to by ŚŚ. This verse points out the contradiction

[[P139]] 126

in Lakṣmī’s being the cause of creation (including those of trees) and destruction involving punishment of offenders in different types of hells on one hand and Her being the Puruṣakāra and Mother on the other.

The creation of trees etc. (the lower orders of plant kingdom such as shrubs and creepers) is a kind of punishment inflicted on certain beings. Destruction of certain individuals and the creation of various types of hells, also imply nigraha on the part of the creator, whoever it be. It is true that the nigraha of the creator, is based upon the sins of the concerned beings. Now the question is, can Lakṣmī ever be imagined even, to be the cause of such creations. The very word ‘Vṛkṣādi’ of the Kārikā points out the absurdity of Lakṣmī’s being their creator. All this is at what is called the ‘Vyaṣṭi’ (individual) level. It may therefore be stated that creation and destruction of beings at the ‘Samaṣṭi’ (collective) level does not smack of nigraha at all, and hence Lakṣmī’s creatorship at that level may be acceptable.

In fact the Kārikā of PM ‘śaktiḥ śriyo’stu’ which is going to be explained later on, suggests that Lakṣmī is capable of such an act, which normally results from nigraha. But what is emphatically denied is that she has cosmic

[[P140]] 127

functions on par with Her husband. This has been emphasised by the Pramāṇas and the traditional teachings. This is also in keeping with the essential character of Lakṣmī.

ŚŚ in this context quotes the ŚTS and refutes it on the following issue. VR observes that the nigraha of Lakṣmī cannot be construed through what is called Pratikūla-sṛṣṭi (creation of trees etc., which is not favoured). According to him creation cannot be treated as being pratikūla at all. Creation means ‘giving birth’, which means associating a soul with a specific body. This also suggests the expansion or spread of knowledge in a corresponding degree. This association with a body and the rise of knowledge cannot be described as unfavourable to the jīva concerned, argues VR. But for a person who is intensely desirous of getting liberated, his body may become pratikūla at that stage only; but at the time of its production it was not pratikūla. On the other hand for one who remained almost like an insentient entity (acit) before creation, getting a body itself has to be construed as a puruṣārtha.

ŚŚ refutes this view thus - one cannot conclude that association with a body in general which gives rise to

[[P141]] 128

knowledge at a particular level itself becomes pratikūla to a given being. E.g., the bodies of divine beings and men giving rise to different degrees of knowledge cannot be considered as being unfavourable (pratikūla) to the concerned beings. In the case of trees and plants, the bodies they give give very little room for the rise of knowledge in those beings. In such cases, those bodies may be considered as being pratikūla. VR’s statement concerning a person with an intense desire for liberation is out of context, says ŚŚ. Such a state is possible only in the case of men who are subject to śāstraic injunctions. ‘How can one’s body become pratikūla even in the state of mumukṣā?’ asks ŚŚ. NM opines that if Lakṣmī were to be accepted as creating these lower orders such as plants and trees, then she may have to be understood as having nigraha.

Another objection raised by VR is also stated and answered by ŚŚ in this context. VR argues that since the creation of trees etc. forms a source of misery for the beings concerned it should not even be willed by the Divine Mother. That is against her status as the Mother. Even a remote association with such a saṅkalpa undermines

[[P142]] 129

Her benign nature. Her giving the necessary permission to the Lord and even prompting Him to carry on such creations do not fit in Lakṣmī’s personality, according to VR.

ŚŚ answers that Lakṣmī cannot be charged with nigraha on the ground that she is responsible for the result of creations which ultimately results in the misery of the concerned beings. Any attempt to connect Lakṣmī with cosmic activities - directly or indirectly then becomes unjustified and useless. What is intended by PM is that Lakṣmī, if accepted as creating trees etc. and as bringing in dissolution at the vyaṣṭi-level, and also as creating hells with all the tortures, then she has to be admitted as having nigraha. What is wrong in it? If she is really doing all that, she must be accepted as having the will (Saṅkalpa) to subject certain beings to suffering and agony. If Lakṣmī, who is declared by the Śāstras as not having any nigraha at all, is accepted as permitting or prompting the Lord to show nigraha, then it becomes a contradiction. Therefore, the only answer that can be given is that Lakṣmī does not herself have any desire to punish anybody, but indirectly such a thing may be attributed to Her. Or it may also be explained that creation of trees, hell, etc. done by the Lord is passively permitted by Lakṣmī, i.e. remaining

[[P143]] 130

‘indifferent’ (upekṣā) on such occasions. ‘Indifference’ means remaining neutral to a thing without showing interest or disinterest. Therefore if Lakṣmī remains as a passive spectator, it cannot be construed as an act of nigraha.

Another argument of VR’s also discounted by ŚŚ. According to VR, Lakṣmī’s non-involvement as creator in the cosmic activities should be understood only with reference to vyaṣṭi-sṛṣṭi i.e., individual creation. But on the collective side, since all the jīvas before creation remain ‘dormant’ as in deep sleep, their creation or even dissolution does not indicate her pratikūlatva (in as much as they are all insensitive to any suffering). This however should not make us forget Her causal character because all the ‘capacity’ therefor is latent in Her, argues VR.

ŚŚ criticises this view on the following lines: Nowhere has NM denied Lakṣmī’s agency - either for the vyaṣṭi-sṛṣṭi or samaṣṭi-sṛṣṭi or samaṣṭi-saṁhāra. Nor has he stated anywhere that Lakṣmī does not have the capacity to do so. What all he stresses is that she does not have ’that kind of causal character’ which is present in the Lord. In the light of this all objections raised earlier are set aside, points out ŚŚ.

[[P144]] 131

ŚŚ also answers a question as to how the terms ‘sarvaloka-maheśvarī’ (supreme ruler of all the worlds) and niyantrī (controller) which point to her niyantṛtva, fail to show her as the cause of the entire universe. He states that Deśika had already indicated the method of interpreting such expressions in his Gadyādhikāra. Even Rāvaṇa the vilest sinner had been treated by the Divine Mother like a lunatic son (उन्मादपुत्र इव श्वत्, p.134) and was kindly advised to make friends with Rāma, who is merciful to all who surrender to Him. She taught him the greatest secret that surrendering to Rāma was open to all. But anyway he did not heed to her advice and ruined himself. Deśika suggests that by becoming the innermost controller of all the beings out of her unconditioned affection and love, the Divine Mother exercises her control (niyamana) by tendering timely advice. That is why she is referred to as niyantrī and Maheśvarī.

The succeeding Kārikā ‘ajnāta-nigrahāyasca’ etc.,181 is introduced by Śrīśaileśa with the prima facie view that Lakṣmī should be accepted as having nigraha like the Lord because terms like niyantrī and Maheśvarī are in support. Further, the Lord also is known for His compassion, unmotivated friendship etc. for the beings,

[[P145]] 132

although He is accepted on all hands to be a strict disciplinarian. Why not Lakṣmī be accepted in the same way, (i.e. as having both the aspects) is the contention of the Pūrvapakṣin.

In answer ŚŚ states that Lakṣmī is known to be full of compassion with no trace of nigraha. ‘Such being the case if Lakṣmī is represented to have nigraha also like the Lord, what distinction is drawn from the lord?’ retorts Śrīśaileśa. In so far as the auspicious qualities are concerned, they are common between Lord and His consort. But the scriptures assert that Lord is the Father of the creation,the ruler of all, chastiser of the wicked etc. Therefore, showing nigraha becomes a natural trait of the Lord. When we speak of His filial qualities such as compassion, parental love and universal friendship, we must take care that the nigraha-element in Him is not overlooked. But in the case of the Divine Mother the very same scriptures assert Her qualities of unmotivated grace and spontaneous mediatorship. So in the case of Lakṣmī, the quality which make Her distinct from the Lord is Puruṣakāratva. The Sāttvata Saṁhitā passage ‘tadrūpamiśraṁ bhinna-lakṣaṇam’ and the statements of ācāryas like Deśika must all be explained keeping this

[[P146]] 133

particular quality of Lakṣmī in mind. Therefore if Lakṣmī also were to be accepted as punishing the wicked through nigraha, there will not be any difference between Her and the Lord. So the upshot of this discussion is that in as much as nigraha and the consequent niyamana are absent in Lakṣmī, she cannot form the cause of the entire universe like Her husband. Her being the cause of the universe through anugraha, is of course reasonable since there is no contradiction of scriptural texts.

The next Kārikā’Yasmāddevyāḥ’ etc.182 confirms this position of Lakṣmī (that she has no nigraha in her) with reference to Deśika’s commentary on the Śaraṇāgati-gadya (ŚG). The Kārikā states that in as much as Lakṣmī has no ‘taste’ for nigraha at all, she is referred to by Rāmānuja in his Śaraṇāgati-gadya as niravadyā (the faultless one). This has been corroborated by Deśika himself.

ŚŚ in his commentary on this verse quotes profusely from Deśika’s Bhāṣya on Rāmānuja’s ŚG and confirms that Lakṣmī is totally incapable of getting angry. Deśika observes that normally speaking,women, in spite of their loyalty and love to their husbands, still occasionally exhibit bad temper, a sort of aversion to their opinion, short-

[[P147]] 134

sightedness, hasty action, hard-heartedness and a tendency to show nigraha. That being the case, how can anybody with no other hope of protection approach Lakṣmī wholeheartedly? That is why Śrī Rāmānuja calls Lakṣmī niravadyā (the blemishless or spotless one). As for the general statement of women being hard-hearted, fickle-minded etc. that may be applicable only to humans who are conditioned by their own Karma. This cannot therefore be applied to Lakṣmī. In fact the Lakṣmī Tantra,Rāmāyaṇa and other texts declare that Lakṣmī is free from all such defects. Sītā’s warning to Rāvaṇa (Sundarakāṇḍa, 27-20) that she does not reduce Him to ashes by Her power since she does not have the sanction of her Lord makes it clear that even against worst sinners she is not inclined to show Her anger.

In the succeeding four Kārikās ŚŚ raises the Pūrvapakṣa that if Lakṣmī is never known to have nigraha, how can epithets like ‘daitya dānava mardinī’ (one who destroys daityas and dānavas) be applied to Her? The answer is that such epithets are derived from the work Lakṣmī does through Durgā and other ferocious Goddesses. As a matter of fact that ferocity is not due to the saṅkalpa of Lakṣmī at all. On the contrary wherever those Goddesses (other183

[[P148]] 135

than Lakṣmī) are stated to show compassion, it has to be traced to Lakṣmī’s Saṅkalpa. Another question is that if Lakṣmī is said to depend upon the karman of certain beings when punishing them through her aspects like Durgā and Kālī, what distinction could be drawn between herself and the Lord? Because He too is known to take into account the karman of the beings whom He punishes. The line of difference between the Lord and Lakṣmī is that the Lord being the father of the living beings naturally tries to chastise them whenever necessary. Lakṣmī, on the contrary acts as the Mediator between them, being motivated by Her Motherly status. The word kānta-prasāda184 clearly shows the remarkable and overwhelming grace of Lakṣmī, which rules out even a trace of nigraha in Her. This is also clear from the introductory portion of Deśika’s commentary on the Catuśślokī. The point that has been established there is that no causality of Lakṣmī can be attributed with reference to each and every cosmic activity, involving nigraha. There is no dispute in so far as Her causal character streamlined by anugraha is concerned.

[[P149]] 136

The following five and a half Kārikās185 (of which the first one is actually a quotation from Deśika’s TT) explain as to why Lakṣmī cannot be accepted as the agent of all cosmic activities involving nigraha. In fact such a proposition will be the contingency when one takes into consideration the statement of Deśika in Nyāya Siddhāñjana that there is sāmya between the Lord and His consort.

NM states that as Deśika pointed out in his TT, the opening verse of Rāmānuja’s Śrībhāṣya mentioned six characteristics of Brahman.186 187 These qualities, like Brahmatva and Śrīpatitva are found only in the Lord but not in Lakṣmī. If Lakṣmī is the Viśeṣaṇa of the Lord she would participate in His nigraha also. To deny such a contingency NM says that for the pleasure of His consort the Lord will be carrying on the cosmic functions in a sportive way. Deśika in his commentary on the CŚ188 has already stated that because the whole thing is conceived as a divine sport, Lakṣmī may also be said to have a role in it, through indirect relationship.

[[P150]] 137

Explaining these verses ŚŚ points out that the word samastakārya-hetutvaṁ, agency regarding individual destruction, creation of hell etc. are unique to the Lord and are absent in Lakṣmī. The next expression mumukṣubhiḥ upāsyatā also applies to the Lord alone, because being the object of meditation for attaining the Bliss of the full experience of Brahman, caused by the annihilation of all association with material Nature (prakṛti), the latent impressions of beginningless karma caused by avidyā, which are in turn generated by a series of nigrahas consequent to the violation of the Lord’s commands from time immemorial. Only the Brahman can be such an object of meditation. Likewise the power to confer Mokṣa after shedding all nigraha lies only with the Brahman. Being the chief object or import (pradhāna-pratipādyatā) of the Upaniṣads is also applicable to Brahman alone. Though Lakṣmī is His attribute, still the substantive namely the Lord, is relatively more important. There can be no dispute regarding Lakṣmī’s having characteristics where the element of nigraha is absent, but she can never acquire those attributes which characterise the essential nature of Brahman. Summarising the discussion in four mnemonic verses ŚŚ states that being an attribute of Lord Viṣṇu

[[P151]] 138

and having the entire universe as Her body by virtue of Her being the śeṣiṇī along with Her consort, Lakṣmī becomes the agent, the source of Bliss, the object of meditation for attaining that bliss, and the chief goal of attainment. Even regarding nigraha she has the capacity (sāmarthya); she can be the niyantrī (controller of all the activities of the virtuous people). She is also all-pervasive and the universal ruler like Him. Her being subordinate to Him however is by mutual will and understanding. These are the aspects of Lakṣmī mentioned by NM in the above Kārikās.

As for the argument that Deśika’s statement of Sāmya (equality) between the Lord and His consort made in his Nyāyasiddhāñjana should be taken to its logical conclusions regarding Lakṣmī’s causality, ŚŚ points out that Sāmya must be understood in its own limited sense. Deśika himself in his TT clarifies that this Sāmya cannot be total and absolute. Lakṣmī is similar to the Lord in all features and characteristics excepting those essential features which make the Lord the ‘Brahman’.

The discussion then turns to a more important question discussed in the Nyāyasiddhāñjana, namely whether Lakṣmī belongs to the category of the jīvas or

[[P152]] 139

not. The view of the Pūrvapakṣin is that the Nyāyasiddhāñjana mentions eight characteristics of the jīva and four of the Lord. On an impartial observation Lakṣmī is found to possess the characteristics of jīva but not of Īśvara. The seven Kārikās that follow summarise this discussion.189

The definition of Īśvaratva according to NS is: ‘svajñāna-svetara-samastadravyaśarīrakatvam’ (‘possessing everything other than Himself and His knowledge, as the body’).190 This cannot be applied to Lakṣmī at all. The definition that can be applied to Her is ‘śeṣatve sati boddhṛtvam’, (‘being the possessor of knowledge while being subordinate to the Lord’). The Pūrvapakṣin asks for an impartial examination of the characteristics of jīva and Īśvara mentioned by Deśika in his Paramatabhaṅga also to find out whose qualities Lakṣmī shares.The characteristics of jīva mentioned there in are eight-fold ādheyatva (being supported), vidheyatva (being controlled), śeṣatva (being subordinate) and aṇutva (being atomic in

[[P153]] 140

size), each one of which is to be taken severally qualifying cetanatvam (being conscious) and ahaṁtvam (having the cognition of ‘I’).

The characteristics of the Lord are four-fold namely, mumukṣu-upāsyatā (being the object of meditation by those who are desirous of liberation), mokṣa-pradatva (bestowership of emancipation), prāpyatva (being the final goal) and ananyādhāratā (not having anybody else as His support).

It will be quite clear from this that Lakṣmī who forms the body of the Lord depends upon Him. The Lakṣmī-sahasranāma-stotra mentions ‘amṛtadhārā’ as one of the names of Lakṣmī. The explanation for this word is that Lakṣmī is dependent on the Lord who is called amṛta. The same stotra also mentions ‘nirāśrayā’ as yet another name of Lakṣmī. Vedānta Deśika states that this word has to be interpreted like Her another name ‘nissaṅkalpā’, without contradicting statements like ‘śrayate ca paraṁ padam’ mentioned in the Āgamas (She resorts to the Supreme Brahman (paramaṁ padam) or the highest abode). So the word nirāśrayā cannot mean, ‘one who stands alone without anybody’s support’. It may mean ‘one who has no support

[[P154]] 141

other than the Lord’. Likewise the word ‘nissaṅkalpā’ (lit, one who has no will) also has to be explained as ‘one who has no will independent of the Lord’s’.

The NŚ clearly mentions Lakṣmī as the body of the Lord191 in the following way: Lakṣmī can be construed as a different state of existence of the Lord, like the Vyūhas since everything in creation has the Lord as its soul. The manifestation of Lakṣmī should also be taken as a different of state of existence of the Lord Himself motivated by either by the desire of Lakṣmī or by that of the Lord. Śrī Kṛṣṇa Tātārya, author of the commentary Ratnapeṭikā is also quoted by ŚŚ in support.192

The conclusion arrived at is that Lakṣmī and Nārāyaṇa alone constitute the Divine Couple and they are all-pervasive by nature. Being unlimited in Svarūpa, He is to be seen in all the jīvas, but this cannot be applied to Lakṣmī.

In the earlier portion of NŚ it was stated that Lakṣmī does not possess the characteristics of Brahman.

[[P155]] 142

That Lakṣmī does not have any nigraha in her is also a point in this direction. This however, does not mean that Lakṣmī is a jīva. The latter portion of NŚ establishes this point by positing sāmya between the Lord and Lakṣmī. Therefore one has to be careful in arriving at the intention of NŚ regarding the exact status of Lakṣmī. What Deśika exactly intends is that Lakṣmī is coeval with the Lord in all aspects excepting in her having nigraha and in Her not forming the cause of all aspects of creation. In every other feature she is supreme like the Lord Himself.

The succeeding Kārikā193 of NM points out that according to some critics Śrī also becomes the import of the word ‘Brahman’194 because according to them Brahman is characterised as Truth, Knowledge and Infinity (cf. ‘satyaṁ jñānam, anantaṁ Brahma’). NM observes that this view cannot be correct. NM in the latter portion of the Kārikā clarifies this point regarding Lakṣmī’s position.195 This is the final ascertained opinion: The characteristic of ‘Brahman’ namely causality regarding the universe applies only to the Lord

[[P156]] 143

and not to both. Those features which are said to be common to the couple are not the characteristics of Brahman. The sāmya between Lakṣmī and the Lord has been explained in the NŚ without infringing upon the characteristics of Brahman which are clearly enunciated in the Śrutis, Upaniṣads, Brahmasūtra and other texts.

What follows is a criticism made by ŚŚ of certain statements made by VR in his ŚTS. The problem is one of syntactical interpretation and not of any philosophical significance.196 VR interprets VD’s CŚB statements regarding Paramasāmya between the ever-liberated souls and the Lord which does not mean total identity, a point accepted on all hands (cf.‘jagadvyāpāravarjam,’ IV.4.17). Likewise the statement of sāmya made between Lakṣmī and the Lord also has to be accepted with due reservations. The expressions ‘yathā’ and ‘tathā’ which are relative indeclinables, must bring out similarity in all aspects, argues VR.197

Pointing out the correct interpretation of this passage, ŚŚ states that although the liberated souls

[[P157]] 144

are said to be extremely similar to the Lord in terms of jñāna and ānanda, still, they differ from Him by virtue of their dependence and subordination. That they cannot be the chastisers of the wicked (daṇḍadhara) is the point of dissimilarity (Vaiṣamya). Likewise, though Lakṣmī is also said to be similar to the Lord in being the parent, śeṣiṇī, the goal, all-pervasive and so on, still she differs from Him by virtue of Her womanhood, loyalty to Him etc. In Her case also the point of dissimilarity (vaiṣamya) is that she cannot be a punisher of the wicked (daṇḍadhara). ŚŚ likewise finds fault with another statement of ŚTS (p.35) regarding the interpretation of a passage of Deśika.198 The actual point is that there cannot be any comparison between the liberated souls and Lakṣmī. The liberated souls have no place in the context of causality whereas Lakṣmī has such a privilege. But still Lakṣmī is present as a viśeṣaṇa (attribute) which is accepted in all the scriptures. Parāśara’s verse ‘svarūpaṁ svātantryam’ etc. also corroborates this view.199

Another statement of ŚTS (p.35) that ‘Lakṣmī cannot share the qualities of the Brahman and that she possesses the

[[P158]] 145

qualities of Īśvara because the form of the couple with Him’ is also criticised by ŚŚ. ŚŚ obviously make a distinction between mukhyeśvaratva (brahmatva) and Īśvaratva bringing Lakṣmī under the second category. Such a classification is not warranted by any pramāṇa, says ŚŚ. In fact NM whom ŚŚ calls ‘asmadācārya’ (our preceptor) never interprets Deśika in the wrong light. As a matter of fact NM does not attribute all cosmic activities to Lakṣmī although he speaks of other characteristics which are common between them, in the beginning, middle and end of the present text PM. NM has consistently stated that Lakṣmī does not have all the cosmic activities in the light of Deśika’s statement ‘atyantasāmyamapi asyāḥ’ etc. The objection raised in ŚTS (p.36) that the definition of Īśvara given in the NŚ (svijñāna-svetara-dravyaśarīrakatvam) becomes the definition of Pati (Brahman) but not of Īśvara, is also subjected to criticism by ŚŚ. As a matter of fact VR who accepts Deśika’s view,points out that Lakṣmī is Vibhu. He is against the view that Lakṣmī is aṇu. Then, what is the implication of this definition of Īśvara? According to the definition everything other than the Lord and His knowledge forms His body. So Lakṣmī also automatically becomes His śarīra. In other words Lakṣmī is not Vyāpaka like the Lord. Therefore the definition

[[P159]] 146

given to both ‘Pati’ and ‘Patnī’ viz., ‘vyāpakatve sati cetanatvam’ becomes contradicted, because only Pati is Vyāpaka and not the Patnī. Then it has to be replied by VR, that although Vibhutva of Lakṣmī is Deśika’s Siddhānta-view, the definition of Īśvara given by him in the NŚ has been made from the view-point of these who believe that Lakṣmī is aṇu. Then, by the same token, argues ŚŚ, that even according to NM, the definition of Īśvara given by VD has been given from the viewpoint of those who do not believe in the Īśvaratva of Lakṣmī.

The intention of ŚŚ is to show that NM’s understanding of VD’s position is correct and that pointing out defects in his standpoint by VR is not reasonable.
