ŚŚ continuing his criticism of ŚTS (p.36) regarding the ‘definition of definition’ and its application to the definition of Īśvara as understood by NM, observes as follows: The definition of Īśvara ‘Vyāpakatve sati cetanatvam’, is applicable to both the Lord and His consort. The real problem arises only when we say that Lakṣmī has the contradictory qualities of both Īśvara and anīśvara in Her. But there is no contradiction at all according to ŚŚ because of the definition of Īśvara given in the NŚ which is meant to preclude Brahmā, Rudra

[[P160]] 147

and other divine beings from the scope of Lordship because they too come into the picture staking their claims for Lordship. The intention of the passage is not to discuss the status of Lakṣmī either as belonging to the category of Īśvara or that of anīśvara. As a matter of fact a more detailed discussion on Lakṣmī as Īśvara has to be made, and it was taken up by Deśika at a later stage of the NŚ through such passages as ‘śriyā saha tu dāmpatyam’ etc.

ŚŚ contends further that there is no room for anīśvaratva in Lakṣmī as is clear from NM’s declaration ‘siddhaṁ tadubhayecchātaḥ sarvaiśvaryasṛuteḥ dvayoḥ’. According to NM both the Lord and His consort are declared by the Śrutis to be the Lords of the entire universe. But how can both be accepted as rulers at the same time? The answer is that ’their by mutual will’ is responsible for such a status. ŚŚ in this context answers a number of criticisms levelled by ŚTS against NM’s arguments mainly regarding the loopholes in the definition of Īśvara. ŚŚ states that a definition can be two-fold: general and special. The definition ‘Vyāpakatve sati cetanutvam’ etc., is a common definition

[[P161]] 148

of Īśvara whereas ‘svajñāna-svetara-dravya-śarīratvam’ is special, concludes ŚŚ.

ŚŚ points out a number of instances from the PM to show that according to NM, as according to Deśika, Lakṣmī is Īśvarī. Therefore, trying to refute his view by pointing out the presence or absence of definitions of jīva and Īśvara in Lakṣmī by VR is beside the point and unwarranted. At the beginning of the NŚ, sāmya has been posited between Lord and His consort for which criticism has been raised regarding Lakṣmī’s sharing the characteristics of the Brahman. Also, the definition of Īśvara given in the NŚ and the presence and absence of the definition of jīva and Īśvara in Lakṣmī given in Deśika’s Paramata Bhaṅga are also explained. NM in the succeeding Kārikā ‘ata eva anantapadaṁ vyāvṛttiḥ’200 points out the absence of Brahman’s Svarūpa Lakṣaṇa from Lakṣmī as given in the TT. ŚŚ points out that according to Rāmānuja’s commentary on ‘janmādyasya yataḥ’, (Br.Sū. I.1.2) the word ananta indicates the ‘absence of limit’ in the Svarūpa of the Lord from the viewpoint of time, space and other objects. Since the Svarūpa of the Lord

[[P162]] 149

is always qualified, it also becomes infinite (ananta). According to ŚŚ this statement implies that the Svarūpa and guṇas of all the eternal beings are removed from the scope of Brahman because they are all limited. But in the case of Lakṣmī, although Her Svarūpa is unexcelled, she becomes limited by virtue of Her Pāratantrya (dependency on the Lord). This indicates further that even regarding causality, Lakṣmī is excelled by the Lord and thus She stands on a different footing. The Pāratantrya of the jīvas is dependent on the will of the Lord. But the Pāratantrya of Lakṣmī is dependent on the will of both Herself and the Lord. This does not indicate that Lakṣmī is a jīva. Nor does it undermine Her Lordship. What is undisputed is that because Lakṣmī happens to be the consort of the Lord, the mediator between man and God, and the Mother of the universe, she has no cosmic activity which involves nigraha. Since Lakṣmī thus becomes limited in Her guṇa and Svarūpa, lacking as she is in svātantrya and nigraha, she does not have Brahmatva in Her. The word ‘Brahman’ applies only to the Lord because the full implication of Bṛhatva (‘bigness’) from the viewpoint of Svarūpa and guṇa is found only in Him.

[[P163]] 150

The succeeding Kārikā201 points out another reason why Lakṣmī cannot be included in the meaning of the word ‘Brahman’. The Supreme Brahman is alone ananta, from the viewpoint of guṇas and anavadhika-atiśaya (limitless excellence) and from the viewpoint of Svarūpa. This Brahman alone described as the goal (prāpya) in the scriptures, says NM in this Kārikā.202

ŚŚ quotes several passages from the Śrī Bhāṣya and the Śrutaprakāśikā to justify this point. The implication is that Lakṣmī does not come into the picture in so far as the definition of the term ‘Brahman’ is concerned. ŚŚ then takes up statements found in the ŚTŚ which imply a controversy on the meaning of the term ‘Brahman’ (whether Lakṣmī is included in Brahmatva or not), a contradiction which according to ŚŚ does not really exist. NM is purported to have, in his PM, declared and accepted Lakṣmī also as meaning of the word Brahman. This according to ŚŚ, is a baseless allegation. All the ācāryas like Bhāṣyakāra and Vedānta Deśika are unanimous in accepting Lord Puruṣottama alone as the meaning of the word ‘Brahman’, and Lakṣmī does not come into the picture anywhere.

[[P164]] 151

A number of passages from the TT and the Gadya Bhāṣya of Vedānta Deśika are quoted in support. The Pāratantrya of Lakṣmī is not adventitious but natural for Her. In the same way the svātantrya of the Lord is natural but not adventitious. Like the sun becoming unexcelled by virtue of the brilliance of his radiance, the Lord also becomes unexcelled by virtue of His association with Lakṣmī of excellent virtues.

That is to say that if Lakṣmī is unexcelled even by Her Lord, it still adds to the glory of the Lord as unexcelled and unequalled (niḥsamābhyadhika). On the analogy of Prabhā we can also conclude that the dependency and subordinate character of Lakṣmī are natural to Lakṣmī since she is the Patnī of the Lord; and because it is dependent upon Her eternal will, her dependency on the Lord also becomes eternal. The question of sāmya between the Lord and Lakṣmī has already been discussed. Nobody who really understands Deśika would argue that the dependency of Lakṣmī is adventitious (aupādhika) and that Her independence is natural. Deśika’s Bhāṣya on Yāmuna’s Stotraratna makes this point clear. In other words, the Pāratantrya etc., of Lakṣmī are the result of mutual will which is eternal and as such, they are natural (svābhāvika). The word ‘svābhāvika’ means ‘Yāvadātmabhāvitva’,

[[P165]] 152

lasting as long as the soul lasts, which means, ’eternal’ The RTS also establishes that the Pāratantrya of Lakṣmī is eternal.203

ŚŚ also criticises the view of ŚTS that the Lord and Lakṣmī have total similarity regarding their Svarūpa, sthiti and pravṛtti and that both have the same kind of Lordship. As already explained on several occasions, Lakṣmī’s independence is marked by dependence on the Lord’s will. The Lord alone can be described as the really independent Supreme Being by whose Saṅkalpa alone Lakṣmī has attained her status. An analysis of Deśika’s Gadyabhāṣya, TT and NM’s PM establishes this point beyond doubt. ŚŚ also quotes a number of passages from the stotras of Yāmuna, Śrīvatsāṅka and Parāśara Bhaṭṭa in support of this view.

The next Kārikā continues the question of Sāmānādhi-kāraṇya (co-ordinate predication) between Lakṣmī and other objects, driving home the point that though all-pervasive and eternal, she is only ’limited’ (paricchinnā) from the viewpoint of guṇas.204

[[P166]] 153

Lakṣmī like the Lord becomes sarvaśeṣiṇī. Therefore Coordinate Predication e.g., ‘artho viṣṇuh iyaṁ vāṇī’ (the Lord is the meaning and Śrī is the speech) becomes possible.

ŚŚ explains that the word ‘sarvaśeṣitayā’ of the Kārikā must be interpreted as sarvadhārakatayā (‘supporting everything’) but not as ‘sarva niyantṛtayā’ (controlling everything) because Lakṣmī cannot be said to control either through nigraha or anugraha. Because Lakṣmī supports both cit and acit and has them as Her modes, she can be referred to with Coordinate Predication involving all entities other than the Lord. Though she is thus nitya (eternal) and vibhu (all-pervasive) she cannot become the connotation of the word ananta (infinity). ŚŚ explains that although by her Svarūpa and Vibhūti Lakṣmī has no limitation, still what is called as guṇaparyāparyanta (’limitation from the view point of attributes) is possible in the case of Lakṣmī. That is what is meant by the expression ‘paricchinnaiva vastutaḥ’ in the Kārikā.

The next Kārikā205 continues the argument and states that compared to the Lord, Lakṣmī is inferior from

[[P167]] 154

the viewpoint of qualities (guṇa) and activities (vyāpāra).

NM states that although Lakṣmī is all-pervasive, she does not become the creator. Explaining this, ŚŚ says that becoming all-pervasive is not the criterion of creatorship. If it were so, Time which is all pervasive, should also be accepted as the creator, which of course, is absurd. Creatorship means, ‘being the agent of creation’ which again means, ‘being the locus of volition which is favourable for creation’. Time being insentient, cannot be the creator. Posing different alternatives ŚŚ points out that being an ‘all-pervasive conscious being’ (vibhu-cetana) cannot be the qualification required of a creator. That Lakṣmī is inferior to the Lord from the viewpoint of Vyāpāra (activity) may also be understood from a different point of view. Vyāpāra here means nigraha-vyāpāra (‘activity involving nigraha’), which is absent in Lakṣmī. ŚŚ contends that being atomic in size also does not preclude a conscious being from becoming a creator, e.g., Brahmā and others who are206

[[P168]] 155

mentioned in our scriptures as creators in different Kalpas.

The succeeding Kārikā ‘śaktiḥ śriyo’stu’207 again makes it clear that Coordinate Predication between Lakṣmī and the world is possible because (1) she has the entire universe as Her mode (prakāra), (2) she becomes the controller (niyantrī) of all and also because (3) she has the capacity to show nigraha although she never entertains such a will.

Explaining the verse,208 ŚŚ points out that niyantṛtva can be three-fold – through grace, through strictness, and through both. Therefore even if one aspect is present one can become the Controller and this is possible in the case of Lakṣmī, i.e. she can control people through Her grace and benevolence. As a matter of fact this quality has been highlighted in the words of Sītā to Rāvaṇa.209 That she is completely free from cruelty is also clear from another expression of the Rāmāyaṇa.210

[[P169]] 156

So it is clear that Lakṣmī has a desire to show anugraha and also the ‘capacity’ to show nigraha. From both these viewpoints we can call her niyantrī on the basis of which coordinate-predication can be made in a primary sense without twisting the text. This view is supported by tradition and many Pramāṇas such as ‘ubhayādhiṣṭhānaṁ ca ekaṁ śeṣitvam’,211 ‘mukārastu tayor dāsaḥ’ etc.212

The following Kārikā213 brings out the same point in clearer terms. According to ŚŚ, Lakṣmī also becomes ruler (Īśvarī) of the universe on the only ground of having both the Vibhūtis (nitya and līlā) under Her control. On this issue she is on par with the Lord. But in so far as hetutva, upāsyatā, etc. are concerned they apply only to the Brahman but not to Lakṣmī who is only an attribute of the Brahman. The point to be noted is that according to ŚŚ, Lakṣmī cannot become the object of meditation exactly in the manner in which Lord becomes the object of meditation. One prays to the Lord thus -

[[P170]] 157

‘O Lord, Give me a full experience of your self’. ŚŚ contends that although Lakṣmī too becomes an object of meditation, here, because she is an attribute of the Brahman, still she merely helps to remove the nigraha of the Lord and as such, does not become the direct object of meditation.

The next Kārikā214 clarifies that the qualities which are stated to be common between the Lord and His consort cannot be taken as the characteristics of the Brahman.

ŚŚ explains that the characteristics of Brahman such as being the cause of the creation etc. of the universe exist only in that person, who has Brahmatva. So they cannot be found in Lakṣmī. As for the other qualities like being the ruler of the two vibhūtis they can be applied to Lakṣmī also. For this reason, these qualities cannot constitute the characteristics of Brahman. VD has mentioned such common qualities in his texts like the NS. Then what about the passage, ‘anīdavataṁ svadhayā tadekaṁ’ (Ṛg Veda X.129.2), which suggests the existence of Prāṇa

[[P171]] 158

(vital breath) whose effect is referred to by the word ānit at the time of cosmic dissolution? It also speaks of Svadhā to which the Supreme Brahman owes his own existence.

The commentator explains that no vital breath (mukhya-prāṇa) is referred to here. Prior to creation Brahman alone is said to have existed. The contention of the Pūrvapakṣin is that Śreṣṭhaḥ prāṇaḥ which is said to have existed prior to creation must be accepted as a product (kārya), not like the element (Ether). it must be explained on the analogy of souls (ātman).

ŚŚ explains that even for the Pūrvapakṣin, Lakṣmī cannot form the cause of the entire universe, since Brahman alone existed prior to creation to the exclusion of every other being. The question of Lakṣmī’s causality does not arise at all.

The succeeding four Kārikās215 confirm the same view,referring to Deśika’s commentary on the Catuśślokī. The point to be kept in mind is that Lakṣmī cannot be cause of the universe on par with Her Lord.

In his commentary on the CŚ, Deśika takes up the word Svadhā and explains it in four different ways.

[[P172]] 159

On any ground, the chief causal character of the Lord is firmly established.

(1) The word svadhā in some texts, is used as a synonym for Lakṣmī. Still it cannot be argued that the existence of Brahman is dependent on Svadhā, namely Lakṣmī. Brahman depends upon his own self for His existence and this has been accepted and declared so by many Śrutis. Hence the word Svadhā can be explained as ‘svasmin dhīyate’ which means the existence of the Lord which depends upon His own person (Svasmin).

(2) Alternately, the word svadhā can also be explained as ‘svakīyaṁ viśvadhāraṇaṁ’ which means ’the Lord’s own capacity to support the entire universe’.216 This kind of interpretation has been given by Śrī Rāmānuja also in His commentary on the aphorism “sreṣṭaśca” (Brahmasūtra II.4.7).

(3) Even if the word svadhā is taken as referring to Lakṣmī, the passage in question merely points to Her ‘sahayoga’ (co-presence or association) with no implication of involvement in the cosmic activity. This point is corroborated by the Mahābhārata passage ‘ahaṁ svahā svadhācaiva’.

[[P173]] 160

(4) The passage ‘Anīdavātam’ etc., has its import in the remarkable love the Lord has towards His consort Lakṣmī by reason of which He is said to be totally dependent on Her (premapāratantryam).

In the next Kārikā, ‘nirasta kāraṇatvaṁtu śriyo noktam na śaṅkitam’,217 NM asks the scholars to examine the passage ‘ānīt’ etc., impartially and decide whether Lakṣmī could be the cause of the universe. Since there is no logic in favour of Lakṣmī’s causality, the word svadhā doesnot deserve to be interpreted as Śrī, concludes NM.

Even if she exists at the time of cosmic dissolution she need not be taken as jagatkāraṇa because it could lead to the contingency of accepting other factors also as jagatkāraṇa purely on the ground of their prior existence.

In the next Kārikā218 ‘śruti-sūtraiśca samsiddhaiḥ’ etc., NM discusses the question of Lakṣmī becoming the Brahman just because sāmya (similarity) has been posited between the Lord and His consort. This would lead to the

[[P174]] 161

unwarranted position that because Śruti says, ‘nirañjanaḥ paramaṁ sāmyamupaiti’ (Muṇḍaka.Up., 3-1-3) even the liberated soul becomes the Brahman and jagatkāraṇa.

The succeeding Kārikā219 points out that Deśika had already shown in his NŚ the way of understanding sāmya between Lakṣmī and Her consorts without infringing upon the characteristics of Brahman, mentioned in the Śrutis, sūtra,etc.

The next two Kārikās220 mention the characteristics which are common between Lakṣmī and Her Lord, which make their dāmpatya eternal.

Qualities like ādheyatva (dependence), īśitavyatva (being the ruled) and śeṣatva (being subordinate), which are found in Lakṣmī make Her the body of the Lord and hence a kārya. Then the question will be raised as to how the divine body of the Lord which is known to be eternal cannot be a kārya. ŚŚ answers that the Śrutaprakāśikā answers this question as to how, though being

[[P175]] 162

a kārya the Lord’s body is still nitya as is the case of the ever-liberated souls (nityamukta) and the Nitya Vibhūti accepted in the sampradāya.

Although Lakṣmī thus becomes a kārya being the śarīra of the Lord, she is still said to be similar with the Lord. As a matter of fact kāryatva and sāmya are mutually inconsistent. Still Deśika has explained the cases of sāmya, aikya, śaktitva, tadvattā etc., referred to in scriptures with the golden principle of dāmpatya between Śrī and Viṣṇu. Because Śrī has been specifically mentioned here as forming a couple with the Lord, ŚŚ contends that she is superior to other consorts like Bhūmi and Nīlā. Because the dāmpatya between Śrī and Viṣṇu is eternal, there is no difficulty in explaining sāmya and aikya between them.

The next Kārikā221 mentions such instances where sāmya has been referred to in scriptures. The passage ‘tasya śaktidvayaṁ tādṛk’ (‘He has two such powers’) is taken from the Sāttvata Saṁhitā. ‘yasyāste’ is a reference222

[[P176]] 163

to v.2 of Yāmuna’s Catuśślokī which also speaks of similarity. Satya,jñāna, ananta etc., are qualities which are common between the Lord and Śrī as in the case of the ever-liberated souls. Whatever be the case, there is no contradiction in the Lord and Lakṣmī forming a couple. Although in some places Lakṣmī and nityamuktas seem to be on the same footing (by virtue of jñāna, ānanda, etc) she is still distinct from them being the Mother of the universe, its mistress, object of refuge and ultimate goal. This forms the content of the next Kārikā.223

NM observes that the sāmya between the Lord and His consort consists in their being the Parents of the creatures and the like and that this distinguishes the ever-liberated souls who are also said to be having sāmya with the Lord. NM makes a suggested reference to Raṅga Rāmānuja’s commentary on NŚ where pitṛtva is explained as janakatva (being the producers).224

ŚŚ explains that the word janaka used by Raṅga Rāmānuja no doubt refers to the parent but still, it

[[P177]] 164

does not suit the context. Lakṣmī cannot be said to have existed along with Brahman prior to creation, in the status of a parent. She merely exists as an attribute and hence Kāraṇatva cannot be attributed to Her.225 This point has already been referred to.

The next Kārikā226 points out that even as the word janaka is interpreted in a secondary sense to mean a parent, the word jagat in the compound jagajjanakatva etc., should also denote the conscious beings, but not the entire universe including the insentient beings also. Explaining, ŚŚ points out that in Rāmānuja’s ŚG also, the expression ‘akhilajaganmātaram’ means ’the mother of all the living beings’. Only then pitṛtva will be common to both the Lord and His consort.227

In the same Kārikā, NM further observes that in the Dvandva Compound, ‘jagajjanakatva - śeṣitva śaraṇyatva - prāpyatvādi-sāmyācca’, the word ‘jagat’ happens to be the first member. By the rule ‘dvandvāt pūrvaṁ śrūyamāṇaṁ padaṁ pratyekam abhisambadhyate’ (‘A word heard at the beginning

[[P178]] 165

of the Dvandva Compound must be construed severally with all the members of the Compound’), it has to be understood only as the sentient, but not the insentient entities as well. Only then the words, ‘janakatva’, ‘śeṣitva’, ‘śaraṇyatva’ and ‘prāpyatva’ become significant.

The next Kārikā228 explains the point by an analogy. NM says that in the word ‘Nārāyaṇa’ of the Aṣṭākṣarī-mantra, the word ‘nāra’ means (a) multitudes of living beings and (b) all things associated with them. The word ‘ayana’ also means, (a) the upāya and (b) upeya, since upāyatva and upeyatva being the ‘means’ and ‘goal of attainment’ become applicable only for living beings but not inanimate entities. So the word ‘nārāḥ’ must be taken to mean only the ’living beings’. On the same analogy, in the expression ‘jagjjanakatva-śeṣitva’ etc., the word ‘jagat’ must be interpreted as ’living beings’ but not as ‘inanimate matter’ because the later sense cannot be syntactically connected with ‘janakatva’, ‘śaraṇyatva’ etc.

In the following Kārikā229 ŚŚ explains that direct janakatva with regard to the universe in its entirety

[[P179]] 166

is found in the Lord only, whereas in the case of Lakṣmī it can be traced indirectly by virtue of Her sharing the sportive joy of creation along with Her Lord. In any case ‘Janakatva’ is common between the two only in this sense.

The sāmya cannot be from the view-point of qualities like jñāna and ānanda. Expressions like Viṣṇupatnī and Śrīpati ascribe svāmitva to both the husband and wife with reference to the Universe. Therefore there is sāmya but no guṇapradhāna-relation (secondary-primary relationship between them).

The following two Kārikās230 discuss the same issue of sāmya. According to some, there is sāmya between the Lord and His wife in being the masters with reference to nitya and līlāvibhūtis. But all other sāmya is based on their mutual śeṣatva implied by the words pati and patnī (in śrīpati and viṣṇupatnī). In other words sāmya is understood as śeṣitva which is two-fold: (a) with reference to the two vibhūtis and (b) with reference one another in being husband and wife. As regards their being the masters of the two Vibhūtis,there is scriptural evidence and hence there is no room for doubt. But their mutual śeṣitva

[[P180]] 167

implied by the words ‘pati’, ‘patnī’ has to be carefully analysed, says NM. That means, there is no scriptural authority to show that Lord becomes subordinate to the other, although the reverse is possible. To explain the passage ‘hrīśca te lakṣmīśca patnyau’ (Tai.Āraṇya. III. 13.2) that Lakṣmī is śeṣa to the Lord. But there is no express statement to the effect that Viṣṇu is subordinate to Lakṣmī.

It may be argued that expressions like ‘śriyāpatiḥ’ and ‘Viṣṇupatnī’ show mutual sāmya between both Lord and His consort, but they do not indicate that one is subordinate to the other.

The word ‘pati’ and ‘patnī’ normally indicate ‘svāmitva’. Therefore, the view that one is subordinate and the other superior, cannot be maintained. This view has been refuted by ŚŚ quoting the Sūtra, ‘liṅgaviśeṣa-nirdeśāt’ (Pūrva.Mīm. VI.I.6) and Śabara’s commentary thereon. ŚŚ points out that ‘patnī’ is technically a woman who has a right to participate in the sacrificial performance of her husband and by the same token, she shares in all the merits that her husband can claim. She has full rights over the dravya acquired by her husband. By this interpretation, ‘pati’ and ‘patnī’ became the

[[P181]] 168

rightful owners of any entity or property. Therefore there can be no contradiction in one becoming subordinate to the other. This is the way in which all statements of sāmya have been justified by VD in his NŚ and other texts.

In the following Kārikā,231 NM following Deśika, shows the method of accounting for statements which speak of ‘oneness’ (aikya) between the Lord and His consort. He says that the ‘aikya’ mentioned in the śrutis between the liberated souls and the Brahman is on the ground of their having one and the same Prakāra or mode. On the same analogy, we can understand prakāraikya (‘oneness of the mode’) subsisting between the Lord and Lakṣmī. This ‘aikya’ (oneness) may be: (1) due to the oneness of the mode brought in by the extreme similarity which is possible between husband and wife; or (2) due to the oneness of Prakāra understood as the śeṣatva that this couple has with reference to the entire creation including the nitya and līlāvibhūtis or (3) it can also be understood as ‘oneness of prakāra’ in forming the deities intended to be the recepients of the ‘havis’ in the form of all the souls

[[P182]] 169

(ātmahaviḥ).

ŚŚ quotes relevant passages from the NŚ232 to support this view. He explains that there are several śruti-passages such as ‘Brahmaveda Brahmaiva bhavati’ (Tai.Up. I.2.1) and ‘nirañjanaḥ paramaṁ sāmyamupaiti’ (Muṇḍ.Up., 3.1.3) which indicate that one who sheds the mortal coil becomes free from nāma and rūpa, brought in by the association with prakṛti. In such a state one can merely be referred to as ‘having knowledge as his form’ (jñānam eva ākāraḥ) and thus form the Prakāra of the Brahman. The word prakāraikya consists in referring to one entity as being identical with another entity (which is of course, a secondary usage) as when we say, ‘so’yaṁ gauḥ’ (‘he is a bull’). ŚŚ argues that statements which refer to the oneness of Lakṣmī and Nārāyaṇa can also be understood through prakāraikya. This prakāraikya can again be understood from three different angles as pointed out earlier.

The discussion on ‘oneness of mode’ (prakāraikya) between the Lord and His consort is continued in the next Kārikā also.233 NM says that the word ‘prakāraikya’

[[P183]] 170

should be first of all construed with the preceding expression quite naturally. Without this, connecting it with the succeeding passage does not make any sense. ŚŚ points out that in the original passage of NŚ,234 similarity between Nārāyaṇa and Lakṣmī who form the couple should be explained through prakāraikya alone and this prakāraikya must be in terms of qualities like jñāna and ānanda. Although there is difference between the jñāna and ānanda of Lakṣmī and those of the Lord, we have to take into consideration the sausādṛśya (extreme similarity) between the jñānas of Lakṣmī and Viṣṇu and also between their ānandas. It is this extreme similarity that facilitates treatment of their jñānas as being one and identical, and ānandas also as becoming one and identical. This leads to the intended prakāraikya on the basis of which the ‘aikya’ of the couple can be satisfactorily accounted for.

ŚŚ winds up the discussion on prakāraikya and remarks that the method of interpretation shown so far applies to ‘statements of oneness’ (aikyavāda) found in authoritative texts. It does not apply to statements of oneness which have no scriptural authority at all, and

[[P184]] 171

which one comes across very often.

The following four Kārikās235 continue the discussion on the ‘aikya’ between Lakṣmī and Nārāyaṇa.

VD’s verses forming part of his commentary on the first verse of the Catuśślokī are quoted as authority regarding the interpretations of text mentioning the identity of Lord and His consort. ŚŚ points out that the CŚB takes up the issue of ‘oneness of Lakṣmī and Nārāyaṇa’ and solves it through what he calls sāmarasya (having identical tastes and mental inclination). But in the NŚ this aikya has been explained as three types of prakāraikya.

There are some critics who argue that it is cumbersome to accept the Divine couple Lakṣmī Nārāyaṇa as two persons and as such it will be parsimonious to accept one single one. NM argues that if parsimony is the only criterion, then the plurality of jīvas can be dismissed and only one jīva should be accepted, which theory however is rejected by Śrī Rāmānuja.

[[P185]] 172

There are also some who argue that all the living beings are both different and non-different from one another. On this view, Lakṣmī and Nārāyaṇa can also be accepted as one. But this view is rejected by the traditionalists. Statements involving abheda (non-difference) between Lord and Lakṣmī can be explained like the statement ‘Rāmasugrīvayoraikyam’ without undermining the essential difference between each other.

ŚŚ states that Deśika has already proved the difference between the Lord and His consort. Texts like ‘naranārīmayo hariḥ’ and ‘nārāyaṇātmikāṁ devīm’ found in the Brahmāṇḍa and Kāśyapīyapurāṇas appear to explain the oneness of the Lord and His consort. But the intention of these passages is quite different. They have to be explained in such a way that the svarūpabheda between the Lord and His consort is not ignored. When we say ‘jyotsneva himadīdhiteḥ’ (’like the beams of the Moon’) we mean only the oneness of the Moon who is the locus of the beams. The NŚ of VD as explained by Raṅga Rāmānuja (RR)236 records a number of views on Lakṣmī such as:

[[P186]] 173

(a) The Lord qualified by sattā etc., is alone is termed as Śrī; (b) Bhagavān, who has permanently taken a different feminine form is called Śrī; (c) The Lord Himself for His own enjoyment takes up a female form which is called Śrī, etc. All these views are rejected by the śruti-passage ‘hrīśca te lakṣmīśca patnyau’. (Tai.Ār.III. 13.2) which clearly establishes the difference between the Lord and His consort in the most natural way (‘as husband and wife’). Moreover Yāmuna’s reference as ‘Kāntāste’ (using different Case-endings) supports this view.

In the next Kārikā,237 NM states that the views expressed by the commentator seem to favour the oneness of the Lord and His wife. Some can be explained or justified while others are totally unauthoritative.

Then what about those passages wherein Lakṣmī is stated to be the Śakti of the Lord? The following Kārikā238 explains this point. ŚŚ points out that NŚ shows the way of interpreting passages where Śrī is

[[P187]] 174

identified with the Śakti of the Lord. According to it Śakti forms only the Viśeṣaṇa of the Lord, being His consort. At the time of creation, this Śakti is identified with Lakṣmī and she can be taken as sahakārī kāraṇa because she also has cosmic creation etc., as a sportive activity. The words ‘samāna-niyatayā’, do not mean that Lakṣmī has all cosmic activities as her sport, since she has no nigraha. This expression therefore means ‘sāmarasyena’, as having identical taste. Deśika’s commentary on Rāmānuja’s Gadya is also quoted in support. ŚŚ also observes that inducing the servants to action is done by the kings through their command. Ministers and others induce the kings to action through appeals. Among equals, kings bring in inducement through gifts but in the case of the Lord, Lakṣmī induces Him to action only through sāmarasya as expressed by the following Kārikā.239

In the succeeding Kārikā,240 NM refers to the interpretation of ‘Śakti’ shown by Deśika in his commentary on

[[P188]] 175

the Catuśślokī. According to these quotations which are taken from the Pāñcarātrāgamas, Brahmasūtra and Brāhmapurāṇa, Prakṛti is called Śakti of the Lord. This Prakṛti could be the primordial Nature according to the prima facie view. But according to ŚŚ, śakti being an aspect of Śrī, can also be identified with her.

Another way of understanding the identity of Śrī and Prakṛti according to the next Kārikā241 of NM is by recognising Prakṛti as an aspect of Lakṣmī. Commenting on this verse ŚŚ remarks that Raṅga Rāmānuja in his commentary on NŚ puts forth what is called ‘śaktitva-vāda’ according to which Śrī is same as Prakṛti, which is the Śakti of the Lord. But the interpretation given by NM that Prakṛti is an aspect of Śrī is more welcome than the śaktitva-vāda, concludes ŚŚ.

In the next Kārikā242 NM quotes VD to the effect that Lord Vāsudeva emanates as Saṅkarṣaṇa, Pradyumna and others. In the same way, He assumes different forms like Sītā and Rukmiṇī. The difference between these two

[[P189]] 176

lies in this: (1) Aniruddha and others are emanations of the Lord in essence (svarūpataḥ). Lakṣmī, although she is essentially different from the Lord can still be understood as His aspect. Consequently Sītā, Rukmiṇī and others can also be stated to be identical with the Lord as the aspects of Lakṣmī. In this manner all passages which refer to Lakṣmī as the Śakti, Saṁvit, Ahantā,Icchā etc., can be accounted for. This is the gist of the succeeding Kārikā itself.243

Commenting on this ŚŚ says that statements which identify Śrī with Viṣṇu’s ‘Icchā’, Saṁvit, Ahantā etc. can be interpreted as pointing out the essential nature of the Lord.244 Passages which speak of Lakṣmī as on par with Viṣṇu can be easily explained by virtue of external dāmpatya subsisting between them.245

[[P190]] 177

In the next Kārikā246 NM remarks that passages referring to Sītā, Rukmiṇī and others as different states of existence of the Lord, have already been explained and justified. But a few commentators avoided references to such passages and have not even explained the reason for their silence on this issue.247

In the next Kārikā248 NM observes that Lord Viṣṇu in some texts is referred to as ‘nārīmaya’ (‘of the form of women’). This must be explained on the ground that He is the support of Lakṣmī herself who represents all womanhood. In the same way Lakṣmī is called nārāyaṇātmikā (‘of the form of Lord Nārāyaṇa’) and this must be interpreted on the basis of Her being the consort of the Lord.

Commenting on this ŚŚ observes that passages found in the Brāhma, Kāśyapīya and Viṣṇu Vaibhava are so far accounted for on the lines of interpretation shown by Deśika. He then enters into a very elaborate

[[P191]] 178

discussion on the exact import of the word janakatva found in the compound ‘jagajjanakatva - śaraṇyatva’ etc. As a matter of fact this issue has already been discussed earlier to counter the view of VR that janaktva is not mere pitṛtva but hitapravartakatva (‘conduciveness to bring about welfare’). ŚŚ points out that there is no need to resort to Lakṣaṇā here and the primary meaning can itself be accepted. Since NM in his introductory verse of this text says ‘dampatī janakau vidheḥ’ there is nothing objectionable in accepting Lakṣmī as the utpādikā (’the one who gives birth to beings like Brahmā’). The important difference between VR and NM is that while VR accepts Śrī as the repository of sāmarthya (‘capacity’) to carry out all cosmic activities without any exception, NM believes that since she has no nigraha at all, and since > sāmarthya alone cannot be the criterion of activities, Lakṣmī can be said to form the direct cause of all functions involving anugraha and that she prompts the Lord to function through sāmarasya (‘identity of taste’), and forms the indirect cause regarding cosmic functions involving nigraha. There is nothing wrong in accepting ‘janakatva’ as pitṛtva, explains ŚŚ in his commentary on this Kārikā.

[[P192]] 179

ŚŚ also discusses the issue of Lakṣmī’s being the ruler of the entire universe (Īśvarī) at length and on the authority of NŚ and other texts concludes that there is no ‘fear of dvairājya’ as a consequence. All this is possible because of the special status of Lakṣmī as the patnī of the Lord who is referred to as Īśvara. He again confirms that the definition of Īśvara given in NŚ ‘svajñānasvetara-samastadravya-śarīratvam’ is intended to exclude Brahmā, Rudra and other gods from the scope, but not Lakṣmī.

The main thrust of ŚŚ’s criticism in this elaborate commentary is against the ŚTS of VR, passages from which are taken and refuted sentence by sentence. The passage from the Sāgārthasaṁkṣepa of Śrīrāmaṁiśra referring to the śeṣa-śeṣi-relation between the Lord and His consort is also quoted by ŚŚ in support of the definition of Īśvaratva which is given as ‘Vibhūtidvaya-śeṣitva’ (having the two Vibhūtis as subservient).

In the next Kārikā NM tries to explain the statement of the Viṣṇuvaibhava,249 which seems to refer250

[[P193]] 180

to the Svarūpaikya of the divine couple. ŚŚ quotes Deśika’s Catuśślokī-Bhāṣya which contains a reference to the Viṣṇuvaibhava. According to him Svarūpaikya is not possible literally. The Viṣṇuvaibhava passage refers to Vigrahaikya only and this can be explained through the mutual will of the couple. The concept of Svarūpaikya is opposed to the Śrutis.

Quoting profusely from the Catuśślokī Bhāṣya which establishes the difference in the Svarūpa of Lakṣmī, NM states in the next Kārikā (76ab) that the view of those who argue that Viṣṇu himself assumes the form of Lakṣmī, should be rejected. It is because of the difference between the Lord and His consort in terms of their essential nature, the latter becomes the body of the former. It is only on this ground that the śruti passage, ‘na tat samaścābhyadhikaśca dṛśyate’ (Śve.Up., 6-8) becomes justified. The Kārikā ‘samādhika daridratvam’ etc.,251 proves that the characteristics of Brahman, such as not having any other being as equal or superior, controlling everything other than oneself, and being the refuge of those who are helpless are found only in the Lord but not in both.

[[P194]] 181

ŚŚ discusses the question whether the epithets used in this verse ‘aśaraṇyaśaraṇyatva’ etc. can be applied to Lakṣmī or not and concludes that the kind of śaraṇyatva which is found in the Lord is characterised by conferring the full experience of Ānanda which is again marked by ‘shedding His anger’ caused by the violations of His command perpetuated by the jīvas from time immemorial. in the case of Lakṣmī however, the element of the nigraha is absent. The other aspect namely, granting Bliss in full and thus forming the object of refuge is present in Her. ŚŚ quotes profusely from Deśika’s Gadyabhāṣya and Catuśślokī Bhāṣya to corroborate the points mentioned in the Kārikā.

The discussion then turns to Lord’s becoming the object of refuge for those who are helpless. In the next Kārikā,252 NM points out that VD has explained the way in which Lakṣmī becomes the refuge for those who are unable to find any solace. She becomes helpful in bringing to fruition the nyāsa they do to the Lord for the sake of Mokṣa.

ŚŚ explains that those who, desirous of Mokṣa approach the Lord, there being no other śaraṇya, they

[[P195]] 182

have to resort to Lakṣmī first to attain their objective. The word of Trijatā in the Rāmāyaṇa, “bhartṛsītāmāpi mahato bhayāt” and those of Hanumān, “alameṣā” etc., are quoted in support.

The next Kārikā253 reflects the views of Vyāsārya who also confirms the view that those who cannot directly approach the Lord should first resort to Lakṣmī.

The next Kārikā254 declares that only the Supreme Brahman qualified by Śrī should be resorted to, on the authority of the definition of Prapatti, the Mantra which speaks of it, the Injunction which ordains it and the Āgama texts, Śrī Bhāṣya and the Sampradāya. The definition of Prapatti ‘ananyasādhye’ etc.,255 is attributed to one Bharata Muni. According to this, entrusting one burden to the Lord with a prayerful request to protect, becomes Prapatti. According to a quotation from RTS, the Lord merely expects the mumukṣu to seek Him for protection (’Rakṣāpekṣāṁ pratīkṣate’). Therefore even prārthanā

तदेकोपायता याच्ञा प्रपत्तिः शरणागतिः।।

[[P196]] 183

becomes an aṅga of Prapatti. The Mantra which ordains Prapatti is the Dvaya and the Vidhi which ordains it is the statement ‘māmekaṁ śaraṇaṁ vraja’ of the Gītā (Ch.18-66). Other passages from scriptures and Rāmānuja’s commentary on the Sūtra ‘uṅgupattleścu’ etc.256 are cited by ŚŚ in support. The gist of the discussion is that Lord Nārāyaṇa alone has to be resorted to by those who are desirous of liberation.

The succeeding Kārikā257 explains the role of Lakṣmī as an attribute of the Lord, who earlier has been explained as the person to be resorted to. The whole process of the Lord’s protecting the jīvas is likened to a sacrifice where the Lord forms the Yajamāna with Lakṣmī as His Patnī, and his qualities forming the ṛtviks. Lakṣmī becomes the attribute of the Lord like the guṇas and vigraha of the Lord which also attain the status of attributes only.

In the next Kārikā258 NM says that the Lord’s qualities like Vātsalya, Svāmitva, etc., and the body (śarīra) have their own utility and application in the

[[P197]] 184

act of saving the devotees. The actual relationship of the Patnī, ṛtviks and others with the Yajamāna in the ‘sacrifice of protection’ is what is called the upayoga in the verse. In his commentary ŚŚ quotes from RTS and explains the exact application of this analogy as intended by NM.

Elucidating the idea, ŚŚ states that the Divine form of the Lord is useful in generating a steady love for Him and concentration on Him in His devotees. The utility of Lakṣmī lies in Her doing things favourable to the Lord, by giving Her consent to His activities. This is so because in a sacrifice, the acts of the Yajamāna should be supported by his Patnī. So when the Lord decides to protect the devotees, Lakṣmī’s association with Him should result in Her consenting to this act.

ŚŚ quotes 3 verses which explain the exact role of Lakṣmī as a viśeṣaṇa of the Lord, being ever associated with Him. As a result of this she becomes the recipient of the bhara of those who surrender to the Lord also. According to these verses Lakṣmī’s association with the Lord removes the unapproachability259

[[P198]] 185

(ādhṛṣyatva) of the Lord and generates confidence in those who surrender. Even during the stage of Nyāsa she remains as an attribute, destroys the sins of the devotees, generates a taste in them for the Lord who forms the goal, produces a conviction that Lord alone is the upāya and ensures His grace for them. All this is the outcome of Lakṣmī’s being the Viśeṣaṇa of the Lord. ŚŚ also gives all the etymologies of the word ‘Śrī’ (’śṛṇāti nikhilān doṣān’ etc) mentioned in the Ahirbudhnya Saṁhitā which reflect Her role of Puruṣakāra between man and God, Her position as the Mother of the beings and Her status as the consort to the Lord. Lines from Yāmuna’s Catuśślokī, Deśika’s Bhāṣya thereon,verses from ŚGRK, Rāmāyaṇa, Viṣṇupurāṇa and Upaniṣads like the Kathā are quoted in support of the contention that in Nyāsa, Lakṣmī remains as a viśeṣaṇa.

In the succeeding Kārikā ‘lakṣmyā vidyā viśeṣatve’260 NM raises the pūrvapakṣa that Lakṣmī may become the cause of universe if she is accepted as a viśeṣaṇa of Vidyā (upāsanā) and answers that it is not so.

[[P199]] 186

Lakṣmī does not attain causality like the Lord merely on the ground of Her being the Viśeṣaṇa of the Lord. This is illustrated on the analogy of Indra and other gods mentioned in the Pratardanavidyā in the Upaniṣad.261 There Indra and others become mere Viśeṣaṇas of the Brahman who forms the on this account they do not become jagatkāraṇa like the Lord. Similar is the case with Lakṣmī also, but with a distinction - Indra and others cannot be associated with all cosmic functions and hence Kāraṇatva in their case is ruled out. But Lakṣmī who is associated with the Lord through similar activities, can become the Kāraṇa like the Lord whom she qualifies.

The next verse ‘upalakṣaṇatvapakṣaṇ’ etc.,262 points out that VD in all his works justifies the role of Lakṣmī as a Viśeṣaṇa like the guṇas and vigraha of the Lord, after refuting the view that she forms merely an upalakṣaṇa.

The succeeding two Kārikās263 clarify the point that Lakṣmī is the Viśeṣaṇa of the Lord. Lakṣmī and the

[[P200]] 187

attributes of the Lord such as Vātsalya and Svāmitva do not have any direct relationship with the Bhārasvīkāraṇa (‘accepting the burden’) and Rakṣāsaṅkalpa (’the decision to protect’) which are unique to the Lord. But still both have an intimate upayoga (purpose) in the activities of the Lord. She prompts the Lord to do those acts through a perfect identity of tastes (sāmarasya). Compared to other guṇas, however, sāmarasya is more in Lakṣmī than in the Lord.

Commenting, ŚŚ points out that even Lakṣmī can be the recipient of Bhara and have ‘rakṣāsaṅkalpa’ which consists in bestowing unending Bliss through anugraha, since there is no contradiction in such a conception.

The following Kārikā264 point out that in the case of the Lord’s cosmic activities, Lakṣmī is said to have aikarasya with the Lord. But this cannot be traced to ‘ekasaṅkalpa’, regarding all the cosmic activities, she being known to be free from… ŚŚ points out that the word aikarasya in the Kārikā must be interpreted as ‘sāmarasya’. He refers to Deśika’s quotation of

[[P201]] 188

a verse from Kūreśa265 where the word ‘aikarasya’ is used to convey the idea of Sāmarasya.

In the following pages a very elaborate discussion is made regarding the views of VR on the exact status of Lakṣmī, whether she forms the Puruṣakāra alone, or the upāya also in addition to Puruṣakāratva. The RTS of Deśika is cited in support. ŚŚ states that the ‘Sāmarthya’ of Lakṣmī which is acceptable to both VR and NM has a different connotation for NM. While VR directly tries to relate Sāmarthya to Kriyā and thus makes Lakṣmī ‘sahakartrī’ in the act of protection and tries to establish Her as the upāya. ŚŚ argues that Sāmarthya must necessarily involve kriyā which in the case of Lakṣmī is not possible. That is to say, she cannot directly show nigraha and later shed it as the Lord does. It is better to accept aikarasya as explained by NM which means sāmarasya i.e. identity of tastes and through that Lakṣmī can indirectly be made a co-performer of the duties of Her husband which ultimately will establish Her in direct upāyatva also. ŚŚ makes a big issue of all of this and quotes profusely from Deśika

[[P202]] 189

to prove that his real intention is to establish the upāyatva of Lakṣmī through sāmarasya and not merely through sāmarthya. Even compared to Her role as the Puruṣakāra, Her prompting the Lord to carry out all the cosmic activities in the spirit of sāmarasya is more reasonable to accept, contends ŚŚ. When the exact role of Lakṣmī in granting complete bliss in the manner of Her Lord is beset with problems, it is logical and authoritative to establish that aspect through paramparā-sambandha, he concludes. ŚŚ quotes profusely from STŚ which criticises the opinion of NM on the status of Lakṣmī and refutes its sentence by sentence. The gist of this criticism is the same namely, Lakṣmī has both Puruṣakāratva and upāyatva according to NM and her upāyatva is characterised by sāmarasya but not sāmarthya as contended by VR. Another point stressed by ŚŚ is that apart from Lakṣmī, no other consort of the Lord is ever accepted as Puruṣakāra in the Śrīvaiṣṇava tradition.

Another discussion266 is that Lakṣmī a Viśeṣaṇa can never be equated with qualities which are themselves no

[[P203]] 190

conscious entities. On the other hand, her Viśeṣaṇatva consists in being of the nature of the Supreme Being Himself and thus she plays a distinct and significant role as Puruṣakāra.

The succeeding Kārikā267 clarifies the point which has already been mentioned before viz., that when Lakṣmī becomes the Viśeṣaṇa for the Lord, she becomes the kāraṇa also (indirectly). But as a Viśeṣaṇa she stands on a different footing from other gods like Indra and Brahmā who are also described as the Viśeṣaṇas of the Lord in the Pratardana Vidyā.

ŚŚ points out that objections raised by VR against NM do not stand to reason. NM has pointed out in several places that Lakṣmī, though dependent upon the Lord, can grant mokṣa also by granting sāmya etc., in Kārikās like ‘sāmyapradāna saṅkalpaḥ’.268

In the following Kārikā269 it has been declared that those who are dependent on the Lord cannot have any

[[P204]] 191

saṅkalpa to grant Mokṣa directly and that such a power lies only with Nārāyaṇa, the Lord of Ramā. This verse according to ŚŚ states that Lakṣmī cannot be equated with Brahmā, Rudra and other gods who are totally dependent on the Lord, since they cannot have saṅkalpa to grant mokṣa. According to RTS those gods may sometimes teach others Nyāsa, Upāsanā etc., as a means of Mokṣa, but Lakṣmī has a direct role to play in the scheme of Mokṣa. She becomes the Sahakāriṇī to the Lord when He desires to grant Mokṣa. This sahakāritva is the special prerogative conferred upon Her by the Lord.

NM never interprets texts like “saṁsāraṁpravatariṇīṁ,” etc., relying upon pure logic, as alleged by VR. On the other hand all factors regarding Lakṣmī such as her unalloyed grace which is natural to Her motherly status, and the resultant bestowing of complete bliss which is called Mokṣa, are all explained on the basis of valid scriptural texts.

ŚŚ as usual, takes up certain passages from ŚTS (pp.50,51) which criticise the PM and answers them in all thoroughness. He tries to prove that the excellence of Lakṣmī is not natural (svatassidha) because it is

[[P205]] 192

admitted to be dependent upon the Lord, and this is also meant to please the Lord. Therefore it cannot be ‘as natural as in the case of the Lord’. Even the traditional passage ‘ananyādhīna-kalyāṇam’270 fits in well with the spirit of PM, argues ŚŚ because the auspiciousness of Lakṣmī is dependent upon the Lord and from this view-point she may be said to be dependent upon the Lord. The Guṇabhāva (subordinate position) of Lakṣmī is the result of mutual will (ubhayecchā), even as the auspicious nature of Lakṣmī is dependent on Bhagavān. By this, however Lakṣmī’s greatness cannot be vitiated. On the other hand such a thing adds to the excellence of Lakṣmī. The Divine couple forms the recipient of the offering in the form of the soul (ātmahavis) in such a way that they have equal share in it. ŚŚ quotes a passage from the Siddhamidhyasodhādhikāra of RTS and establishes that certain contradictions pointed by VR in the statements of NM do not really exist at all.

In the next Kārikā271 NM observes that if one carefully analyses the point whether Lakṣmī is Viśeṣaṇa or upalakṣaṇa,

[[P206]] 193

her status as upāya also would have been understood. Commenting on this ŚŚ says that Lakṣmī’s upāyatva is clearly established in the Mūlamantrādhikāra of RTS, NŚ and the Nyāsa Tilaka of VD. Substantiating his statements with a number of quotations from these texts, he also points out the untenability of the objections raised by VR.

In the following verse272 NM states that Lakṣmī’s being the upāya like the Lord is not ‘heard’ (’through any scriptural declarations’) at all because she is free from nigraha. That she is capable of conferring the bliss of Mokṣa (ānandānubhava) through anugraha is accepted on all hands. Deśika in his RTS explains kopanivṛtti as ‘pāpebhyaḥ mokṣaṇam’. The fact that Lakṣmī makes one free from sins itself implies her absence of anger. It is this kind of upāyatva that is possible with Lakṣmī.

The following Kārikā273 explains the same point. The universal Mother can never afford to get angry. The Lord alone becomes the daṇḍadhara. This again has to be traced to the violation of the divine commands by the jīvas in some remote past. Deśika in his RTS has time

[[P207]] 194

and again declared that the śeṣatva of Lakṣmī covers every living being in the universe apart from the Lord and that Her grace is bereft of any trace of anger. By the statement ‘na māturanapādyate’ (it does not behove the Divine Mother) what NM wants to convey is that Lakṣmī cannot be the means of liberation after ‘shedding of anger’ (kopanivṛtti-pūrvaka) etc., which feature is unique with the Lord. ‘viśiṣṭa-niṣedha’ has its import in viśeṣaṇa-niṣedha (when a substantive which is qualified is totally negated, the intention is to negate the attribute alone). Citing parallels from the sacrificial parlance such as “lohitoṣṇīṣāḥ ṛtvijaḥ pracaranti” (ṛtviks, wearing red turbans, move about) and ‘dadhnā juhuyāt’,(‘one should offer curds in the fire’) ŚŚ points out that the stress is on lauhitya (redness) in the first instance and on curds in the second, which form the viśeṣaṇa. Therefore nigraha-nivṛtti is of great importance in this context,argues ŚŚ. Deśika also cites the well-known passage ‘yathā na kriyate jyotsnā’ to assert that removal of the impediments is the chief criterion of the upāyatva of Lakṣmī.

The Kārikā ‘asyāśca’ etc., points out that the pārārthya of Lakṣmī (’that she exists exclusively for274

[[P208]] 195

the Lord) is dependent upon the desire of Lord alone or on their mutual will. There are śruti-passages in favour of both of them being the rulers of this universe.

The Kārikā ‘sā tu nārāyaṇasyaiva’275 explains in clear terms that Lord Nārāyaṇa, consort of Ramā alone has the direct Saṅkalpa to confer Mokṣa, who is independent. The opening statement of the Rahasyaratnāvalīhṛdaya of Deśika illustrates this point, says NM.276

The word Nārāyaṇa has been explained by ŚŚ as Tatpuruṣa and Bahuvrīhi compounds, bringing out the suzerainty of the Lord and his total independence.

The passage from RRI referred to,277 brings out the same idea that Lord Nārāyaṇa alone is totally independent in removing all the impediments and that He does not depend upon anybody else in this matter.

NM appeals to critics to analyse the statements of Deśika found in the RRI, Catuśślokī Bhāṣya and Gadyabhāṣya

[[P209]] 196

and come to a conclusion regarding the essential nature of Lakṣmī. Lakṣmī can grant all rewards directly or indirectly. Her magnanimity is reflected in expression like ‘Sarvakāmapradāṁ’ etc.

ŚŚ points out in his commentary that although complete experience of the Brahman is quite natural to jīva as brilliance is to a gem, it still depends upon the Saṅkalpa of the Lord. Though it is natural all the time, still the aspect of its leading to a continuous and unbroken service of the Lord has to be aspired for by the jīvas. Thus it becomes a puruṣārtha and God’s Saṅkalpa becomes invariable for its attainment. Quoting a verse from RTS, ŚŚ says that like a father granting a share in property to his son after his formal request although he rightfully deserves it, the Lord grants Kaiṅkarya to an offending jīva only after his formal prayer. It is this kind of Saṅkalpa that is referred to before.

The discussion then shifts to the status of Śrī as the Viśeṣaṇa of the Lord who is called the ‘siddhopāya’. “How can anyone state that Śrī becomes an ‘upalakṣaṇa’ (Indicator) in the first portion of the Dvayamantra?”

[[P210]] 197

asks Nārāyaṇa Muni in the next Kārikā.278 The Siddhopāya-śodhanādhikāra (of the RTS), the Gadyabhāṣya and the Catuśślokībhāṣya of Deśika do not prove Lakṣmī as either an Upalakṣaṇa or as an upāya. Their intention is to show Her as a Viśeṣaṇa of the Lord. ŚŚ objects to VR’s allegation that NM equates Lakṣmī with other ‘pāratantra-cetanas’ and makes her devoid of ‘subhāśrayatva’. What NM states is that Śrī has no direct desire to confer mokṣa like the Lord. He never denies her ‘subhāśrayatva’. The point to be noted is that the ‘upāyatva’ of Lakṣmī lies in Her ‘conferring the experience of complete bliss’, whereas the ‘upāyatva’ of the Lord consists in His conferring such an experience ‘after shedding his wrath’. There is no question of any ‘duality’ of upāyas. NM has been consistent in this declaration, says ŚŚ in his commentary.

The next verse of the PM states that the ‘pārārthya’ of Śrī is based on the will of the Lord. Since the śrutis declare that both the Lord and His consort are the ‘rulers of all’ (sarvaiśvarya), it must be concluded that the ‘pārārthya’ of Śrī is dependent upon the will of both.279

[[P211]] 198

Commenting on this ŚŚ explains the relation between the Lord and His consort, quoting the Viṣṇusahasranāma-bhāṣya (p.560) of Parāśara Bhaṭṭa, on the word ‘Śrīdhara’. The relation is comparable to the one subsisting between a gem and its radiance, a flower and its fragrance, the Moon and her beams and nectar and its sweetness, which are all natural (autpattika). Śrī is an ‘apṛthaksiddha-dharma’ dependent upon the Lord. Her relation with the Lord exists as long as She exists, which means it is ’eternal’ and ’natural’.

ŚŚ, as usual, takes up passages from the ŚTS,280 purporting to criticise the PM and answers that nowhere does NM contradict the statements of VD regarding the status of Lakṣmī as the inseparable ‘Viśeṣaṇa’ of the Lord. He discusses at great length that Lakṣmī cannot have even the desire to set the beings free (mokṣaṇa-saṅkalpa of the form ‘mokṣayiṣyāmi’) since that would imply Her ‘binding’ the jīvas first. He points out that Śrī can become the means of liberation by removing ‘avidyā’ (avidyānivṛttikartṛtvarūpa-mokṣopāyatvam) in which aspect she is similar to the Lord. He illustrates

[[P212]] 199

this point by profuse quotations from Deśika’s RTS (Caramaślokādhikāra) and Śaraṇāgati-Dīpikā (v.3).

ŚŚ also states that NM has not just advocated the ‘puruṣakāratva’ of Lakṣmī. He has also proved that she becomes the ‘upāya’ in a number of Kārikās (e.g., ‘sakṣātparamparāto vā’). He has also stated that She, like the Lord, becomes the object (uddeśya) of Bharanyāsa. He finds fault with VR that ascribing views to NM which are not actually stated by him, is unfair and unfounded.281

It may then be asked as to how the definition of the term ‘śrī’ as ‘śṛṇāti nikhilān doṣān’ does not imply the desire on the part of Śrī to ’eschow nigraha’. The reply is that in the earlier portion of the Dvayamantra, the interpretations given for the word śrī become significant to establish the ‘upāyatva’ of the Lord and this is clearly stated so in the RTS. ‘Removing or destroying all the doṣas’ means ‘destroying karmas which stand as impediments in the path of those who aspire to practise the Upāya’. In other words, She destroys the impediments of upāya and contributes to the full emergence of ‘upāya’.

[[P213]] 200

By the interpretation of Śrī as ‘Śṛṇoti’ (‘she listens to’), Her status as Puruṣakāra is established. Of the six interpretations for the term ‘śrī’ given in the tradition, three are useful in establishing the Lord’s ‘upāyatva’, while three are useful to establish her ‘prāpyatva’. Since she does not have ‘upāyatā’ characterised by the absence of ‘nigraha’, she does not become the content of the word ‘Brahman’. That is why this aspect has not been mentioned in the definitions of the term ‘śrī’, contends ŚŚ.282

Introducing the next Kārikā283 ŚŚ says that since the ‘puruṣakāratva’ and ‘nityayoga’ are acceptable on all hands, there would not have been any speciality about the PM if it were to repeat the same points. The special distinction of this work of NM lies in the fact that Lakṣmī has been explained as an upāya through Her status as Viśeṣaṇa but not as the chief upāya like the Lord. This kind of Viśeṣaṇatva has been illustrated by VD in his RTS and Nyāsatilaka.

[[P214]] 201

The following verse284 states that Lakṣmī’s status as Viśeṣaṇa has been clarified by Deśika with the help of illustrations taken from the Śrutis.

Explaining, ŚŚ points out that Deśika in his Nyāsa Tilaka (V.4) has given the example of the expression ‘mahendra’ to illustrate Lakṣmī’s relationship with the Lord as Viśeṣaṇa. The other illustration given by Deśika is of Agni and Viṣṇu who become the ‘devatādvandva’ to receive the offerings in a fire-sacrifice called ‘Āgnāvaiṣṇavam’. The difference between those two examples is that in the first instance, ‘mahat’, becomes the Viśeṣaṇa of Indra, and it is insentient. In the second illustration, Agni who becomes the Viśeṣaṇa of Viṣṇu is a conscious being (Cetanā). In the other example ‘Vṛtro vṛtraṇighātināṁ, vṛtraḥ indraḥ’,Vṛtraḥ who is the Viśeṣaṇa of Indra is also a conscious being. Therefore Kumāra Varada, in his commentary on the verse under question states that on the same analogy Lakṣmī also can become an attribute of the Lord.

In the example of Agni and Viṣṇu by virtue of the Dvandva compound involving ‘itaretara sambandha’, Agni

[[P215]] 202

and Viṣṇu both receive equal importance. This is from the viewpoint of the Samāsa. But compared to Agni, Viṣṇu is superior and on this account between Agni and Viṣṇu the Viśeṣaṇa-viśeṣya relation can be established. This is obtained through the ‘sense’ (artha).

The following verse Vṛddhihrāsa285 states that the same idea of Lakṣmī’s Viśeṣaṇatva is reinforced by the Brahmasūtra,”Vṛddhihrāsa" etc (III.2.20). All the illustrations given to support Lakṣmī’s Viśeṣaṇatva become justified on the analogy of the dṛṣṭāntas, discussed in ‘Vṛddhihrāsa’ etc.

ŚŚ explains that in the Brahmasūtra the aphorism ‘ambuvadagrahaṇāttu na tathātvam’ (III.2.19) raises an objection to the employment of illustrations like the reflection of the sun in reservoirs of water,and that of the face etc., in the mirror, to drive home the point that the Supreme Lord,though present in earth, water, etc., is not affected or associated with the defects found in those places. The subsequent sūtra,’Vṛddhihrāsa’

[[P216]] 203

etc.answers these objections that although there seems to be a disparity between the illustration (dṛṣṭānta) and the illustrated (dārṣṭāntika), strictly speaking there is no such thing when one takes the ultimate import of the illustrations.

Illustrations need not be taken to correspond to the illustrated in all aspects. Even a partial similarity will serve the purpose. Ether may be present in a big vessel or small vessel. Still it is not affected by bigness or smallness of the adjunct. The Sun may be reflected in reservoirs of water which may have different shapes, but still he cannot be associated with those shapes, small or big. It is in that aspect that the position of Lord as existing in pṛthivī etc., has to be understood. That partial similarity can also be employed is clear from the illustrations “simho māṇavakaḥ” (‘student is a lion’). So the Lord who has ubhayaliṅga, (“freedom from defects and possession of perfections”) can never be tainted by any defect by virtue of His physical presence in different locations.

ŚŚ points out in his commentary that on the analogy of these, one can also conclude that all the particulars

[[P217]] 204

mentioned in the illustrations by Deśika, such as ‘mahendra’, ‘āgnā-viṣṇū’ etc., need not be literally anticipated in the case of Lakṣmī. Mahattva is an attribute of Indra in one case. In the second case, ‘āgnā-viṣṇū’ both Agni and Viṣṇu seem to be equally important but the importance of Viṣṇu compared to Agni is contextual and hence Agni becomes an attribute of Viṣṇu. On the same token, Lakṣmī also becomes a Viśeṣaṇa of the Lord, concludes ŚŚ.

The following verse286 stresses the adjectival character of Lakṣmī. ŚŚ in his commentary brings out the untenability of certain allegations made by VR against NM’s depiction of Lakṣmī’s importance. He quotes profusely from the RTS and Nyāsa Darpaṇa of Deśika to substantiate his argument. The point which he wants to drive home is that the Viśeṣaṇatva of Lakṣmī becomes firmly established if one subjects the PM to a careful examination. When the Lord and His consort are said to become the recipients of the Ātmahavis, Lakṣmī becomes an attribute to the Lord, and this is the position which NM sticks to throughout his work. There is no room for an alternative view.

[[P218]] 205

The next Kārikā287 confirms the same view and adds that the status of Lakṣmī as an attribute of the Lord has been clearly enunciated by Deśika in the Īśvara - section of Nyāyasiddhāñjana. ŚŚ points out that Lakṣmī’s Viśeṣaṇatva does not imply any equality in status between Her and the Lord as may be construed from the examples given viz., “Mahendra” etc.

ŚŚ also refutes the criticism of VR that the third example given by Kumāra Varadācārya to his Nyāsa Tilaka-vyākhyā, namely, “Vṛtraḥ vṛtra-nighātinaḥ” is unwarranted. There is nothing wrong in giving three examples to drive home a point in argument. Another example is ‘Indrasya putripe’ and the distinction between this and ‘vṛtro vṛtra-nighātinaḥ’ lies in this: In the former illustration even when the son is referred to indirectly (in’putriṇaḥ) the Viśeṣaṇatva is not lost. But in the later example, Indra becomes an adjective as the ‘killer of Vṛtra’. One is a direct reference and another is indirect.

In the passages ‘makārastu tayordāsaḥ’, ‘asya mama ca śeṣam hi’ and ‘ubhayādhiṣṭhānaṁ ca’, on the face of it,

[[P219]] 206

the importance of Lakṣmī seems to be on an equal footing with that of the Lord. Therefore doubts about equality of Lakṣmī are possible at the time of one’s offering one’s essential nature to the divine couple (svarūpa-samarpaṇa). But such a question does not arise at the time of performing Bharanyāsa where Lakṣmī becomes an attribute of the Lord and only in that capacity becomes the Uddeśya of Bharasamarpaṇa. The status of Lakṣmī as an upāya, which prompts one’s doing Bharanyāsa to the Lord is the result of Her being an attribute of the Lord only. It is this idea that is substantiated in the Kārikā-and-a-half that follow.

Explaining the Kārikā, ŚŚ states that although Lakṣmī and Viṣṇu seem to have equal importance in the Yajña involving ‘ātmahavis’, Lakṣmī becomes an adjective to the Lord the ‘śaraṇya’,at the time of Bharanyāsa. This is clear from a number of passages of the Rāmāyaṇa, Sāttvatasaṁhitā, Viṣṇusahasranāma-stotra and the stotras of Ācāryas like Yāmuna and Parāśara.288 ŚŚ clarifies that Nyāsa is of three kinds: Svarūpanyāsa (offering one’s essential nature), Bharanyāsa (repositing one’s burden)

[[P220]] 207

and Phalanyāsa (offering the fruit of one’s endeavour). In all these, the PM proves that Lakṣmī is an Attribute of the Lord, but never the chief factor (pradhāna) like the Lord.

The question that is raised289 is whether there is any difference between Bharanyāsa and Ātma (svarūpa) Nyāsa. Answering in the positive, ŚŚ says that those who are desirous of mokṣa alone perform Ātmanyāsa (or Svarūpanyāsa) and Phalanyāsa, whereas all others (desirous of other fruits) perform Bharanyāsa. ŚŚ also criticises the view of ‘some modern critics’ (’ādhunikaḥ’) that the Lord and Lakṣmī both become important as the uddeśya with regard to Svarūpanyāsa and that for Bharanyāsa, it is not so (i.e. only the Lord becomes the recipient and thus attains importance).

ŚŚ refutes the view of VR that the word ‘Dampatī’ indicates the equal status of husband and wife forming the couple. Varadācārya in his commentary on Nyāsatilaka observes that with reference to people like us, both Śrī and Her Lord always become the śeṣins. But since the Lord is the master of all, He becomes the śeṣin for Lakṣmī also. So

[[P221]] 208

while the Lord is the Master of all, Śrī becomes the Mistress of all excepting One (i.e. the Lord)’. VR argues that both the Lord and Lakṣmī are equally important (samaprādhānya) while NM is in favour the relative importance of the Lord. The view of VR is against the view of Deśika, who refers to the Lord as ‘śriyāḥpati’ thereby implying the secondary status of Śrī. In several sections of his RTS such as Arthapañcakādhikāra, Tattvatrayādhikāra, Siddhopāyasodhanādhikāra, Paripūrṇabrahmānubhavādhikāra, Mūlamantrādhikāra, Dvayādhikāra and the Caramaślokādhikāra, Śrī is shown as the Viśeṣaṇa of the Lord and hence her lesser importance (compared to the Lord) is established beyond all doubt, contends ŚŚ. He cites several passages from all these sections mentioned above, to corroborate his viewpoint. In his unduly elaborate criticism, he tries to vindicate his Ācārya’s position in this way: His Ācārya i.e., NM nowhere accords equal importance to Śrī. She is only an Attribute of the Lord, in which capacity alone she can be the object of Prapatti, whatever type of Prapatti it be - Svarūpa, Bhara or Phala. Nowhere she becomes the ‘Uddeśya’ like the Lord. Whether she is the upāya or upeya, She remains as the Viśeṣaṇa of the Lord only. What NM does not accept is the status of Lakṣmī as an Upalakṣaṇa of the Lord.

[[P222]] 209

In the next verse290 NM observes that even as Viṣṇu becomes the recipient of the offerings in the ‘Āgnā-vaiṣṇava’ sacrifice being the Inner Controller of Agni, in the sacrifice of ‘ātmahavis’ also, the Lord becomes the recipient, forming the inner controller even of His consort Lakṣmī.

The next verse291 anticipates another argument that when ‘maudgacam’ is offered to Śrī, the recipient, viz., Śrī, becomes the ‘Uddeśya’. In the case of ‘ātmahavis’ also let Śrī become the chief object of offerings. NM points out that even in the offering of ‘maudgacam’, Śrī is not the chief recipient. Viṣṇu who is the inner controller of Śrī becomes the ‘Uddeśya’ there. Even in the offering of ‘caru’ to Aditi, Viṣṇu becomes the recipient of it as the inner controller of Aditi.

The next two verses292 anticipate the question that if Śrī has the Lord as her soul, it must be so stated by the Ācārya (Deśika) and that such a position is not clear from Deśika’s work. For this the reply is

[[P223]] 210

given that in the motif of Lakṣmī (Lakṣmī-yantra), Lakṣmī alone is considered to be more important than the Lord. In the same way in the Sudarśana-yantra also, Sudarśana (the chief weapon of the Lord Viṣṇu) is recognised as more important than Viṣṇu himself. But still Deśika in his NŚ has established that even these instances ultimately culminate in the Supremacy of Lord Viṣṇu alone who happens to be the ‘antaryāmin’ of Lakṣmī, Sudarśana and others who are worshipped in different yantras for different purposes by different aspirants.

It may still be argued that Lakṣmī can be accepted as the direct recipient and uddeśya of ‘Ātmahavis’ and that she need not be taken as forming the uddeśya through Viṣṇu, her Inner Controller.

ŚŚ introducing the next Kārikā293 answers the above objections by saying that at the very outset of the text PM, NM declared that Lord Viṣṇu the consort of Śrī alone forms the cause of the universe, that He alone has to be resorted to for liberation and that He becomes the

[[P224]] 211

protector as well as the goal along with Lakṣmī.294 The present Kārikā now concludes the discussion by driving home the same point in almost identical terms. ŚŚ quotes several earlier Kārikās of the PM and declares that Lakṣmī remains an attribute of the Lord in all manifestations (avatāras), that she is secondary to Him and that in that capacity alone she becomes the upāya. She becomes the recipient of ‘ātmahavis’ along with Bhagavān as inner-controller, and not independently. In support of his contention, NM in the following Kārikā295 quotes the declarations of Vedānta Deśika. According to Deśika, the consort of Śrī (Śrīmān) is all-independent. He is the Master and in all conditions, He does not stand in need of anybody else. This kind of self-dependency or independence culminating in His Svāmyam cannot be found with anyboly else.

As contrasted with this, the position of Lakṣmī is always marked by dependence on the Lord, she being an attribute which is always subservient to the substantive. Her status as upāya can only be understood within the given framework of subservience to the Lord.

[[P225]] 212

The succeeding verse296 states that when the Lord wants to protect somebody, His grace qualified by His independence becomes the chief cause therefor. His being the Svāmin, the eligibility of the person, the ‘nyāsa’ he performs etc, all become co-operative causes. ŚŚ comments that by referring to the Lord as Puruṣārthashetu, NM suggest that Śrī who becomes the Viśeṣaṇa is subordinate, and to that extent Her role becomes secondary.

The Kārikā297 quoted earlier clearly states that Brahman’s upāyatva is emphasised in the definition of Prapatti, the Mantra which pertains to it (Dvayamantra), the sentence which ordains it (Caramaśloka), other passages, the commentaries and tradition. The word upāyatva of the Kārikā refers to the chief upāya. Brahman alone becomes the chief upāya and Lakṣmī the secondary upāya, points out NM.

The next verse298 confirms the same contention that Lakṣmī merely forms an attribute of the Lord like His guṇas and vigraha (divine body). The Caramaśloka

[[P226]] 213

(Gītā XVIII.66) has the word ekam which,according to some, refers to the numerical oneness of the person who is resorted to,namely the Lord. But even then Lakṣmī’s presence as an Attribute cannot be denied, concludes ŚŚ.

Quoting Deśika’s two verses,299 NM questions as to why critics do not relish the relation between Śrī and Her consort as an attribute and a substantive, who form a single śeṣi-principle, with identity of taste (aikarasya) in all functions. She becomes the Viśeṣaṇa, though devoid of the Saṅkalpa to protect, and devoid of the acceptance of Bhara (Bhārasvīkāra). In his commentary on these verses ŚŚ observes that the Dvayādhikāra of RTS proves this point. The Dvayamantra itself is the pramāṇa which corroborates this view.

The following two Kārikās300 are the verses of Deśika (RTS, p.362) which NM quotes in support of his own statements made in the next two verses.

The question whether Lakṣmī a cetana can form an attribute of another cetana has been answered by

[[P227]] 214

Deśika by referring to the Pratardana Vidyā of the Upaniṣad.301 Therein, Indra and others are said to be the attributes of the Paramātman, who exists as their indwelling spirit. Therefore even a cetana can become a Viśeṣaṇa like any other Viśeṣaṇa which normally is acetana.

But nowhere should Lakṣmī be denigrated to the level of an upalakṣaṇa. Even in the state of Bharanyāsa she becomes an attribute of the śaraṇya. This has been confirmed by a quotation from Deśika: ‘svāmyupāya upeyāśca’ etc.302

The distinction between the three kinds of Nyāsa, Svarūpa, Bhara and Phala which has been mentioned earlier is again stated for the sake of emphasis by NM.

That what Deśika has stated in the verse ‘prāmuktānāṁ’ and ‘api cādivaṁ’ in his commentary on the Catuśślokī303 has been quoted by NM to confirm the Puruṣakāratva of Lakṣmī and Her eternal relationship with the Lord which status she gets by mutual will.

[[P228]] 215

Another verse ‘Jñānabhogaḥ’ of Deśika304 is quoted to show the distinction between Lakṣmī and nityasūris, a point which has already been referred to. The verse ‘Nyāsānāṁ prasādam ca’305 points out that Nyāsa becomes possible due to the Saṅkalpa of Her Lord which is confirmed by the verse ‘upāyadānam etc’. of Deśika.306 According to ŚŚ, the word upāyadānam indicates the Puruṣa-kāratva of Lakṣmī. He quotes the verse ‘Arthasvabhāvā’ of Nikṣeparakṣā to support Lakṣmī’s Puruṣakāratva. And in the succeeding verse ‘Viśeṣaṇā-viśeṣeṇa’ etc.,307 NM states that only the Supreme Brahman qualified by Lakṣmī who has three aspects (ākāratraya) is accepted as upāya of Mokṣa in this system. ŚŚ clarifies that the three aspects of Lakṣmī (ākāratraya) are: (1) niru-pādhika-śeṣitva (being the mistress of everything without any limiting adjunct) which is a synonym of Īśvaratva (Lordship); (2) Vibhūtidvaya-śeṣitva (mastery over the two vibhūtis); (3) Tanniyantṛtva (being the controller of these vibhūtis). By these special features

[[P229]] 216

Lakṣmī becomes superior to the three kinds of jīvas, (baddha, mukta and nitya) who are servants of the Supreme Lord and also to the ajīvatattva (acit). This is the purport of the next, Kārikā ‘nirupādhika-śeṣitva’ etc.308

The next Kārikā ‘yadicchayaiva’ etc.,309 declares that Lakṣmī belongs to Īśvarakoṭi and not jīvakoṭi because the Lord commands (rules) and chastises all the beings only according to the wish and for the pleasure of Lakṣmī. It is therefore logical to conclude that such a Lakṣmī for whose sake the Lord does all this must belong to a category different from that of the jīvas.

The following verse ‘eketarā’310 points out even if Lakṣmī becomes part of the Īśvara as His attribute, there is no fear of dvairājya (having duality of rulers). The problem of dvairājya arises only when rulership is vested in two different persons. But as pointed out in the next verse ‘prabhāditya-prakāreṇa’,311 the relation

[[P230]] 217

between Śrī and the Lord is like the relation between radiance (prabhā) and the Sun. Here one adds to the excellence of another and there is no other entity which effects that excellence. There is therefore inseparable relationship (apṛthaksiddhatva) between the Lord and His consort which again confirms the adjectival character of Śrī.

The verse ‘ananyadevatā’ etc.312 clarifies that one who is desirous of salvation has only one deity, one upāya, and one sādhya (the Lord Viṣṇu). But still, doing Śaraṇāgati to Lakṣmī is acceptable to Lord Himself and as such, supreme one-pointedness by Him is not affected. This is what Deśika says in his Gadya Bhāṣya. This is also illustrated by another analogy: worshipping Ananta, Garuḍa, Viṣvaksena etc., which are all attendants of the Supreme Lord does not mitigate the value of Supreme onepointedness towards the Lord. Such is the case of Lakṣmī also who is the Viśeṣaṇa of the Lord.

In the next verse313 NM states that all the verses so far quoted from “Śrīmān upto ‘ananyadevatā’

[[P231]] 218

etc., are taken from Śrī Deśika’s RTS, Catuśślokī-bhāṣya, Gadya Bhāṣya and Nikṣepa Rakṣā. In his commentary ŚŚ shows which verses are taken from which text of Deśika and also adds a few more works from which NM. has quoted to substantiate his views. They are Paramārthastuti, Śrīstuti (of VD), Śrīstava (of Kūreśa), Śrī Raṅgarāja-stava and Śrīguṇaratnakośa (of Parāśara Bhaṭṭa).

The following fifteen verses from “Catuśślokyādhikārānte” upto “upāyuktāṁśa-vaiśadyāt” enumerate the five views stated by Deśika in his CŚB regarding the essential nature and status of Lakṣmī.

NM states that since five views are mentioned by Deśika, each preceding view being over-ruled by the succeeding one, ordinary people will be confused as to which particular view Deśika personally advocates. He adds that where more than two or three views have been expressed by authors, it is conventional to take the last mentioned one as the personal view of the author. This is the practice followed in the Vākyānvaya-section of Śrī Bhāṣya. The fact that Lord alone is the cause of the entire Universe is common to all these views. Still, since He engages in the cosmic activity for the

[[P232]] 219

pleasure of His consort Lakṣmī, she also, is considered to be the cause of the Universe.

Of these five views the first one holds that Śrī is aṇu (atomic) in size. The second, third and fourth views maintain that she is all-pervasive. The third and fifth views are mutually at variance regarding the subordinate status of Lakṣmī being caused by the will of the Lord, according to the will of the both. ŚŚ in his commentary goes into a very elaborate and detailed discussion (from p. to ) on these different views. He makes an in-depth study of these views, giving a logical introduction, and quoting relevant authorities in support of each view. He shows the logical developments of these views in the order of enumeration and points out the subtleties of each view, highlighting their differences and correspondences. It may be mentioned that the interpretation of five views made by ŚŚ forms his distinct contribution to the development of the concept of Śrī because as NM has already pointed out, the Catuśślokī-adhikāra of Deśika cannot be understood easily by people of ordinary intellect.

While explaining these views ŚŚ also refutes the criticism of ŚTS, levelled against NM’s text. The chief

[[P233]] 220

objection raised by ŚTS is that PM of NM presents Lakṣmī as Puruṣakāra but not as an upāya. ŚŚ answers that this is wrong and unfounded because NM has, on the authority of Deśika, established Lakṣmī not only as Puruṣakāra, but also as upāya, prāpya and the like.

In the middle of this discussion there is a lacuna of twelve palm-leaves of the manuscript (folio 165 to 177) and we are therefore, not in a position to surmise what ŚŚ had discussed therein.

In the text of the Maṇidīpikā i.e. (available after the break) we find the reply given by ŚŚ to VR, regarding another point.314 It is regarding the Sāmarthya (capacity or power) of the Lord by virtue of which even the Puruṣakāra of Lakṣmī becomes feasible and possible.
